Contract or Task Order Title This PWS defines requirements for the Contractor to provide dark fiber, equipment, and commercial facilities to support Department of Defense (DoD) users in the Continental United States (CONUS). This PWS further defines requirements for the Contractor to install, integrate, and test Optical Line Amplifier (OLA), Junction, and service delivery node (SDN) equipment and provide Operations and Maintenance (O&M) support in commercial fiber facilities. In addition, this PWS defines the requirements for the Contractor to provide end-to-end transmission and professional support services to include, but not limited to, Defense Information Systems Network (DISN) diversity and resiliency capabilities, system integration, and system upgrades. 3. Background

Attachment 1, PWS Page 1 of 28 Pages

The Defense Systems Information Agency (DISA) provides world-wide telecommunications services to the Department of Defense, Other Government Agencies, and mission partners throughout the world to meet various missions and requirements. 4. Objectives This PWS includes a new Indefeasible Right of Use (IRU) fiber optic link along with the installation of various telecommunications equipment at new facilities. The work shall effectively include the purchase of new equipment and installation of said equipment at the targeted facilities where the IRU fiber strands intersect. The Optical Transport Network will be 100 Gigabyte/second ("100G") 6500 Packet-Optical Transport Network (P-OTN) and tie into the current DISN. This work will provide network connectivity to additional DoD sites to meet one of DISA's missions of providing telecommunications services to the DoD, Other Government Agencies, and mission partners throughout the world to meet various missions and requirements. 5. Scope The scope of this PWS includes all services and supplies necessary to perform the objective, to include programmatic, engineering, and other technical services and the procurement of all necessary equipment and components. The work and services to be performed shall be subject to the requirements and standards contained in the following: o o o This PWS and any other materials included in the Request for Proposal file Contractor's technical and cost proposal In the event of a conflict between the PWS and the Contractor's proposal(s), the PWS will control

6. Performance Requirements The task areas under this contract are provided below. ˇ Task Area - 1: Program management, reporting, meetings and reviews The Contractor shall provide the program planning, design, coordination, control, and reporting. ˇ Task Area - 2: Implementation of a new 100G P-OTN segment The Contractor shall Engineer, Furnish, Install, Secure, and Test (EFIST) and make operational a new 100G 6500 P-OTN consisting of fiber, amplifier and SDN locations detailed in the CONUS Site Specific Manufacturing Bill of Materials (MBOM) (Attachment J2). MBOM provided as Attachment J2 is based on expected engineering and may change based on fiber characterization data provided by the awarded Contractor. Equipment purchases in Attachment J2 will include an extended 3-year Manufacturer's warranty with Next Business Day (NBD) advanced parts replacement coverage. This coverage should include the Manufacturer's 24 x 7 Technical Support service and access to the Manufacturer's Global Technical Support Center for administering support incidents. The 3-year extended warranty should also include the Manufacturer's software subscription called Smart Support. Smart Support includes software upgrades at no cost during the period of performance as well as full software technical support and bug fix support. Contractor equipment purchases in Attachment J2 will become government furnished equipment (GFE).

Attachment 1, PWS Page 2 of 28 Pages

The Government, in conjunction with technology refreshing its current transport network to 100 Gbps (P-OTN), will be adding new sites with the same capabilities and monitoring systems. The fiber network must provide for a robust, flexible, long-term solution for dedicated infrastructure, diverse route connectivity, transmission and integration services, equipment and capabilities necessary to provide the data transport needs of the DoD. The Contractor must provide acceptable tested and IRU 2 fiber strands from: o Tinker Air Force Base (AFB), OK Building 3900 or 3001. From Tinker AFB the route must connect to Fort Sill, OK Building 1645 or 462. If Building 1645 is chosen as the starting point above, the route must continue from Fort Sill, OK, Building 462 and connect to Barksdale AFB, LA (Building 3447 or 7212). If Building 462 is chosen as the starting point above, the route must continue from Fort Sill, OK, Building 1645 and connect to Barksdale AFB, LA (Building 3447 or 7212). From Barksdale AFB, LA the route must connect to Fort Polk, LA (Building 1830). From Fort Polk, LA the route must terminate at Keesler AFB, MS (Building 1101).

The Contractor must provide full turnkey implementation EFIST of Ciena 6500 equipment on the IRU fiber compatible with the current 100Gbps P-OTN. ˇ Task Area - 3: Operation and Maintenance and Sustainment services for fiber and associated assets The Contractor shall provide and perform all the requirements necessary for sustainment of all IRU assets and associated co-location facilities and equipment. This entails, but may not be limited to, backbone fiber, associated co-location facilities, and end-to-end transmission for (SDNs) including GFE equipment within commercial and Government facilities. Task Area 1- Program management, reporting, meetings and reviews 6.1 PROGRAM MANAGEMENT 6.1.1 Initial Project Review (IPR)

Upon award the Contractor shall conduct an Initial Project Review (IPR) to present the project plan to include, but not limited to, the project schedule, programmatic requirements, technical requirements, and implementation schedule for the requirement. The review shall be conducted 30 days after authorization to proceed and should also include a discussion of any known risks, unresolved issues, and problems as well as mitigation strategies. The Contractor shall support the following in preparation for the meeting: ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ Coordinate location requirements and logistics necessary to conduct the meeting Identify issues, problems, and/or opportunities to improve services and systems Track and report installation progress to date Prepare and submit meeting minutes

The exact date(s) and location(s) will be determined through coordination between the Government and the Contractor. All subsequent status updates will be reported in the Monthly Progress Report.

DELIVERABLE 001: Initial Project Review DELIVERABLE 002: IPR Meeting Minutes DELIVERABLE 003: Monthly Progress Report

6.1.2

Comprehensive Implementation Plan

The Contractor shall develop a Comprehensive Implementation Plan (CIP) to integrate and manage activities associated with implementing any equipment modifications to the existing infrastructure. The Contractor's CIP shall define procedures, specific approaches, and schedules required to complete the implementation activities listed below ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ Survey, engineer, and accomplish pre-installation activities related to the preparing the fiber, e.g., fiber testing and splicing to GFE lateral fibers and site (hut/ central office) specific support services, e.g., HVAC, power, backup power, access control, etc. Perform site preparation Obtain approvals and permits Implement fiber network Operate and maintain the installed fiber and equipment

The CIP shall include all aspects, to include supplier provided end-to-end services and integration of DISN diversity and resiliency capabilities. 6.1.2.1 Security The CIP shall include a section that details the approach for implementing physical security and information assurance requirements detailed in this PWS and the Functional Requirements Specification (FRS) (Attachment J3). As part of the Comprehensive Implementation Plan (CIP), the Contractor shall include a security implementation plan, which provides a documentation trail. As part of the site surveys, the Contractor shall document its ability to accommodate the security requirements that are contained herein. 6.1.2.2 Site Notification The CIP shall include a section that identifies the Contractor's approach for notifying the site personnel of pending installations and pending Contractor-conducted testing. The CIP shall also describe the approach for resolving issues at the site during the installation and testing period. 6.1.2.3 Risk Management The CIP shall include a risk management section detailing how the Contractor manages program risk throughout the life of the program. This section shall address the Contractor's risk management practices,

Attachment 1, PWS Page 4 of 28 Pages

mitigation strategy and mechanisms for controlling resources and schedules. Risk items include potential delays associated with Contractor/subcontractors performance and construction permits.

6.1.2.4 Project Schedule The Contractor shall include a schedule for completing the work contained in the associated PWS task, including all required reviews and testing. This schedule shall identify milestones for all facets of engineering and implementation. The Contractor's implementation schedule shall conform to the priorities established by the Government. The CIP shall address the process to accommodate schedule changes caused by disruptions. The schedule shall be developed in coordination with the Government. The Contractor shall notify the Government 30 days in advance of any changes so the Government can coordinate the schedule impact. DELIVERABLE 004: Comprehensive Implementation Plan DELIVERABLE 005: Project Schedule 6.2 FIBER TESTING The Contractor shall provide detailed test plans and procedures for supporting fiber and equipment installation acceptance. The Contractor shall test all DISN fiber by span from one Fiber Service Delivery Point (FSDP) to adjacent FSDP. Prior to purchase of fiber specific optical equipment, the Contractor shall complete fiber attenuation testing for each fiber span designed to employ P-OTN equipment. The P-OTN equipment requires accurate measurements of the fiber loss between amplifiers for successful amplifier operation. DELIVERABLE 006: Fiber Test Plans and Procedures DELIVERABLE 007: Fiber Test Results 6.3 EQUIPMENT INSTALLATION DESIGN The Contractor shall develop an Engineering Design Package (EDP) per amp and SDN site for completing installation of equipment in the Contractor and Government facilities on the new fiber backbone. The EDP will contain site-specific information for installing the equipment prior to integration into the fiber backbone. The Contractor shall perform the installation, configuration and testing of the equipment based on their EDPs. The Contractor shall include the final installation and configuration details of each amp and SDN site in the as-built drawings and documentation. All installation related materials (IRM) shall be provided by the Contractor. Jumper connections between the equipment and the fiber shall be appropriate for the 6500 P-OTN equipment. The equipment shall be installed in strict accordance with the equipment manufactures detailed installation procedures. At Government Service Delivery Node (SDN) locations, equipment must also be installed in accordance with the DISN Implementation Standards dated 30 Jan 2013 (Attachment J4). The Contractor shall acquire any required permits and approvals necessary for the installation. The Contractor shall deliver on CD in Adobe pdf "As Built" drawings and documentation showing the final configuration and placement of Government equipment in all facilities.

Attachment 1, PWS Page 5 of 28 Pages

DELIVARABLE 008: Engineering Design Package DELIVERABLE 009: As-Built Drawings 6.3.1 Optical Equipment Testing

The Contractor will perform P-OTN testing between Government Services Delivery Nodes (SDN). The P-OTN consists of OLA equipment and associated channel specific equipment such as terminals, regenerators, and Reconfigurable Optical Add Drop Multiplexers (ROADM) located at the SDN and Junction Nodes. The testing will evaluate all equipment on the link. All test data (including updates) shall be documented and provided to the Government no later than 10 days after testing or update, as applicable. DELIVERABLE 010: OLA & SDN Test Data 6.4 SYSTEM INTEGRATION The Contractor will integrate the OLA and SDN sites with the fiber and the network management elements into a complete operating system. The Contractor shall lead in the integration effort with assistance from the Government Network Support Center (GNSC). The Contractor shall work together with the GNSC team during integration and provide on-call troubleshooting, repair, and technical expertise support of the backbone, access fiber, and fiber facilities. Integration support may require Contractor persons being at several different fiber, OLA, or SDN locations at the same time. System integration support will terminate when Full Operational Capability (FOC) is declared and the P-OTN network is successfully installed, tested, and integrated with Government approval. The Government reserves its right to witness any testing. The Contractor shall provide a minimum of ten working days' notice prior to conducting any acceptance testing. The Contractor shall perform necessary adjustments or corrections to any service deficiencies prior to Government acceptance. Government personnel and/or representative access to the Contractor's facilities shall be arranged by the Contractor to support this activity. DELIVERABLE 011: Network Acceptance Test Results Task Area 2 - Implementation of a new 100G P-OTN segment 6.5 GENERAL CONTRACT REQUIREMENTS The following section provides additional requirements and technical specifications that apply to this contract. This section also provides fiber and equipment installation and implementation procedures and requirements. This section also includes network management and information assurance requirements. The Contractor shall adhere to all prevailing telecommunications industry standards for the work required herein, and to any unique Government requirements as stipulated within any attachments to the contract. FOC shall be achieved for the work contained herein and is defined as: complete and satisfactory delivery of this required service, in accordance with all of the conditions of this PWS and associated contract. Government approval of the Contractor's test results shall be deemed the final compliance step to attain FOC.

Attachment 1, PWS Page 6 of 28 Pages

6.5.1

General Fiber Requirements

The Contractor is expected to ensure the IRU fiber and associated assets remain in compliance with the requirements detailed in this PWS and FRS (Attachment J3). All fiber and equipment installed and implemented under Task Area 2 shall comply with the appropriated subsections under the PWS and the FRS. 6.5.2 Fiber Count

Fiber Optic Cable strands (two) shall be provided between the FSDP identified in Task Area 2. All access fiber installations shall consist of a minimum of 12 strands in a single fully buried duct dedicated for use solely by the Government with one empty duct alongside. These ducts shall be a minimum 50 mm in diameter. If the access fiber exists, then no additional fiber is required. 6.5.3 Definition of the Fiber Service Delivery Point (FSDP)

The FSDP is defined as the fiber patch panel located at the Government/non-Government facilities. Figure 6.5.3 depicts the notional location of the FSDPs. Figure 6.5.3 Depiction of FSDPs and spans (Notional)

6.5.4

Amplifiers and Other Optical/Electrical Transport Equipment

The Contractor shall provide the OLA configurations and OLA equipment designs for each of the Contractor's facilities. The fiber shall work with the proposed P-OTN equipment.

Attachment 1, PWS Page 7 of 28 Pages

DELIVERABLE 012: OLA Configuration and Equipment Design 6.5.5 Signal Reach

The fiber shall support all wavelengths and required transmission rates with a minimum reach of 2000 kilometers without electronic regeneration. 6.5.6 Outside Plant

The Contractor shall be responsible for all permits, environmental compliance requirements, easements, and rights of way. All work shall be done in accordance with the requirements listed in the following sections unless superseded by the local Government regulations. The Contractor shall provide adequate facilities including uninterrupted power, suitable operating environment and required physical security in accordance with FRS Section 1.3, Facilities and Section 1.5.4, Facility Security. Fiber optic cable shall be suitable for the environment in which it is installed and shall adhere to the requirements listed in the FRS unless superseded by the local Government regulations. 6.5.6.1 Required Fiber The Contractor shall provide dark fiber for the fiber "strings" (segments) identified in Task Area 2. The fiber to be furnished between two (2) locations on a string will be a composite of backbone fiber (where available) and two (2) pieces (known as access fiber). An access path's length must not extend farther than the first central office or hut from the base. If new fiber is required for a repair, site relocation, or technology refresh, the base may have existing fiber ducts that can be used for pulling new fiber to some of the locations. For all of the fiber segments that run on base, the Government will work with the Contractor on utilizing existing on-base fiber paths/trenches, if possible. Unless otherwise directed by the Government, all SDNs shall have at least two access paths. For those locations (Base/Post/Camp/Station) that have two nodes (dual node situation) the Contractor shall ensure two separate, diverse paths access these nodes. 6.5.6.2 Fiber Between Dual Nodes on a Base If the Contractor needs to repair or replace existing dark fiber on a Government base between two SDNs, the Contractor shall consult with the appropriate base communications personnel/management (e.g., Army Directorate of Information Management (DOIM) on using existing base conduits, trenches, etc.). The Contractor shall fully coordinate and consult with the appropriate base communications personnel if new fiber is proposed to be trenched on base. 6.5.6.3 Vaults, Manholes, Hand-holes When trenching new fiber paths in order to repair or replace existing dark fiber, the Contractor shall construct manholes and hand-holes to provide access and cable slack points at appropriate points in the fiber path. New facilities of these types shall be constructed in a manner that meets or exceeds the Contractor's existing construction standards used in the network. These facilities shall be resistant to tampering and vandalism. Vaults, manholes, and/or hand-holes shall be sited at regular intervals, where necessary for fiber access, splicing, etc. These facilities shall be installed in accordance with the FRS. 6.5.6.4 Underground Installations Direct-burial fiber is not acceptable; a conduit/duct shall protect the fiber. Underground fiber shall be installed in accordance with FRS Section 1.2.7. 6.5.6.5 Aerial Installations Aerial fiber is not acceptable unless Government approval is granted in very limited cases where fully buried cable is not feasible due to environmental, technical, or economic circumstances. In cases where

Attachment 1, PWS Page 9 of 28 Pages

aerial installation is approved by the Government, aerial fiber shall be installed in accordance with FRS Section 1.2.8. 6.5.6.6 Fiber Path Fiber optic cable shall be suitable for the environment in which it is installed, (e.g., aerial installations may be equipped with a jacket designed for UV exposure, underground cable may be gel-filled and suitable for duct installation, etc.) and shall adhere to the requirements listed in the FRS unless superseded by the local Government regulations. The Contractor shall notify the Contracting Officer and Contracting Officer Representative in writing when local regulations supersede the Government requirements as stated in the PWS and/or FRS. All services must adhere to the requirements of the PWS and attachments thereto. The fiber path between any two points shall be the most direct path feasible with regard to geographic obstructions and rights of way. The fiber path shall be installed such that any active network elements along that path (i.e., amplifiers and regenerators) can be passively protected from electromagnetic interference (e.g., noise immunity). 6.5.6.7 Detailed Fiber Maps, Data and Drawings The Contractor shall develop a fiber map (as well as supply Straight Line Diagrams). The map shall identify how the Contractor satisfies all applicable Government connectivity. The fiber map shall contain detailed maps (street level) and drawings that contain or reference data on the type of fiber, depth of installation, date of manufacture, date of installation, Bi-directional Optical Time Domain Reflector (OTDR) trace, Spectrum Analysis, Chromatic Dispersion value at 1550nm, Optical Signal to Noise Ratio (OSNR), length of fiber, number of splices, PMD, easements, rights of way, huts, manholes, hand-holes and Central Office locations. The Contractor shall provide these underlying data (latitude/longitude) using the Visio diagrams and/or spreadsheets. The Contractor shall update the fiber map for any changes as the result of repairing or replacing existing fiber and shall designate if the fiber is existing or new, and if new, if it will be pulled in existing ducts or if it will require trenching. All fiber shall be identified as buried or aerial. Detail of geographic location, distances involved and description of aerial application (construction type and height of aerial poles; metal, wood, high tension, etc.) shall be provided for all aerial fiber segments proposed for the dedicated use of the Government. DELIVERABLE 013: Detailed Fiber Map 6.5.6.8 Splicing and Handling Requirements All splicing shall use fusion-splicing technique. Connectors shall only be present at FSDPs. All connectors shall support the technical requirements as specified in the FRS (1.2.3 Fiber Performance). The Contractor is required to provide ancillary material and consumables for splicing, testing, and related aspects of the fiber implementation. Splicing shall be in accordance with the requirements of the cable manufacturer as well as required splicing and termination/connector loss specified in the FRS (1.2.6 Splicing and Handling Requirements). 6.5.6.9 Facilities The following requirements pertain to enclosures such as Huts / Diversity Intermediate Line Amplifiers (ILAs) parks, amplifier spaces, secure facilities, and any other items that may fall under this category. The spaces or enclosures may be existing or new, and may be used jointly by the Government and the

Attachment 1, PWS Page 10 of 28 Pages

Contractor. Sufficient real estate/floor space shall be provided such that both front and rear access to the installed GFE equipment is possible. If installed in an outdoor enclosure, the enclosure shall be hardened to protect against access and vandalism. If installed in an area adjacent to right-of-way for vehicular traffic (such as roadways, freeways, waterways, or rail lines), the enclosure shall meet the safety standards of the authority having jurisdiction over the right-of-way. Where required by the needs of the equipment, the enclosure shall be furnished with environmental support (heating, cooling, humidity control, dust filtering) on a 24x7x365 basis. Day-to-day power shall be provided and backed up via Uninterruptable Power Supply (UPS). Emergency power shall also be available (in the event of commercial power failure), using battery, UPS, emergency generator systems, or a combination thereof for a minimum of 10 hours while the commercial power is out. The enclosure shall meet the requirements as outlined in FRS Section 1.3. No equipment room, facility, or secure portion of a facility shall display or refer to DoD or Federal ownership of equipment or fiber. The Contractor shall allow the Government to install/implement an out-ofband communications access circuit to Government equipment for management and control purposes. The Contractor shall provide rack space for up to 2 racks in the huts where amplifiers are required by the Government. At regenerator sites, up to 4 rack spaces shall be provided.

6.6 INSTALLATION AND IMPLEMENTATION REQUIREMENTS The following subsections detail implementation and installation requirements for dark fiber and optical equipment when necessary to repair and replace existing fiber. 6.6.1 Environmental Assessment (EA) Survey

The National Environmental Policy Act (NEPA) applies to the United States (includes CONUS, Alaska, Hawaii, and U.S. territories), and directs that all federal agencies give appropriate consideration to the environmental effects of their decision making on major federal actions affecting the quality of the environment. DoD Directive 6050.7, Environmental Effects Abroad of Major DoD Actions (Enclosure 2), directs DoD to a documented decision making process, where proposed actions may result in significant harm to the environment of a foreign nation or protected "global resource." Because the Government must consider the environmental issues in its decision making process, the Contractor shall produce an Environmental Assessment (EA) for each site where new trenching is required to repair or replace existing fiber. Each EA shall fully address the environmental concerns of 40 C.F.R. Parts 1500 through 1508. The EA shall be prepared to facilitate expedited consideration. As a minimum, an EA shall address: 1) the affected environment (40 C.F.R. Section 1502.15), 2) the environmental impact(s) of the proposal (40 C.F.R. Section 1502.16), and 3) a listing of agencies and persons consulted (40 C.F.R. Section 1502.17). See 40 C.F.R., Section 1508.9. When new trenching is required to repair or replace fiber on base, posts, or stations, the Contractor shall contact the office (base, post, or station) responsible for environmental affairs to determine if an EA has been done for the routes planned and, if so, shall utilize the existing EA(s).

Attachment 1, PWS Page 11 of 28 Pages

DELIVERABLE 014: Environmental Assessment 6.6.2 Dark Fiber Installation

6.6.2.1 The Contractor shall be responsible for all aspects of the installation of dark fiber for the DoDIN, including preparation of commercial locations for supporting amplification, and regeneration, according to the requirements given in the FRS (Attachment J3) under this contract. The Contractor shall plan and manage the activities necessary to accomplish all activities undertaken with respect to fiber installation. 6.6.2.2 Fiber installation consists of, but is not limited to, implementation and testing of the fiber links and business management processes. The Contractor shall provide the personnel and plans to accomplish a seamless and expeditious installation at both the Contractor and Government facilities. 6.6.2.3 The Contractor shall include a fiber installation plan as part of the Comprehensive Implementation Plan (CIP). The Contractor shall be responsible for conducting site surveys of all Contractor facilities and the Government sites to validate the ability to accommodate the requirements that are contained herein. 6.6.3 Installation Requirements

Contractor installations shall be in accordance with standard industry practices, standards, and guidelines. The Contractor shall maintain on-site at all times one copy of the as-built drawings. The Contractor shall be responsible for connecting the fiber between the DoDIN SDNs covered by the contract according to the schedule approved by the Government and to the requirements in the FRS. The Contractor shall perform site preparation and inside cabling to complete service delivery. This includes inter-building and intra-building on posts, camps, and stations. 6.6.3.1 FSDP Connection Requirements The Contractor shall be responsible for providing connection from its fiber network to each DoDIN Fiber Service Delivery Point (FSDP). It is permissible to share the patch panels with other users. The Contractor shall obtain rights of way, permit easements, environmental compliance requirements, and approvals for installation of all required DoDIN routes. Installed fiber cables used to transport DoDIN requirements shall fully comply with all requirements of the FRS. 6.6.3.2 Sites Survey Documentation for DoDIN Fiber Installations at Government Facilities The Contractor shall prepare site survey documentation, which identifies any site preparation requirements such as intra and inter facility fiber route drawings and locations that require ducting/trenching, installation and modification of equipment, and facility configurations. Plans, including drawings, shall be complete and conform to industry standards before work permits, digging permits, etc., are issued and installation can start. The Contractor shall be responsible for site preparation work necessary to accomplish fiber delivery. Site preparation includes providing any required interconnect facilities, cabling, and ducts necessary to bring the backbone fiber to the FSDP. The Contractor shall coordinate and receive Government approval to conduct any and all site preparation work at Government facilities. All work done by the Contractor under this contract shall conform to ANSI/TIA-606-B-2012 and ANSI/TIA-607-B-2012; all-appropriate national and local codes, all other directives referenced within this contract, and shall conform to highest commercial industry standard installation and repair practices. All work and code compliance shall be subject to Government review and approval.

Attachment 1, PWS Page 12 of 28 Pages

DELIVERABLE 015: Site Survey Documentation 6.6.3.3 Pulling Cable The Contractor shall not exceed the pulling tensions prescribed by the cable manufacturer specifications at any time when handling and installing cables. The Contractor shall certify in the Test and Acceptance Report that cables installed have not been stressed beyond their specified limits. 6.6.3.4 Approvals and Permits The Contractor shall obtain all local (including base, post, camp, and station approvals) and regional permits and permissions to install fiber and modify facilities necessary to provide DoDIN fiber. At all sites, the building owner's representative shall approve any required changes to the facility. If necessary, the Contractor may request permission to use Government facilities, utilities, service or real estate to support Contractor fiber installation. 6.6.3.5 On Premise Cabling For all installations (unless otherwise required) the Contractor shall provide inside cabling and install appropriate cable cross-connects between the Government and Contractor's patch panels at the FSDP. The Contractor shall coordinate with the building manager and make all arrangements for service installations as the Government's representative. New on-premise cabling to support fiber installation shall conform to the following standards and requirements. In the event the local code exceeds those stated below, the local code shall be followed. Any new on-premise cabling will comply with the following: ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ANSI/TIA -570-C, August 16, 2012 ANSI/TIA-568-C Commercial Building Telecommunications Cabling Standards, February 2009 ANSI/TIA -569-C Commercial Building Standards for Telecommunications Pathways and Spaces, May 3, 2012 ANSI/TIA-606-B Administration Standard for the Telecommunication Infrastructure of Commercial Buildings, June 2012 National Electrical Code NPA-70, October 1999 meeting

The Contractor shall notify the Contracting Officer and Contracting Officer Representative in writing when local code exceeds the standards and requirements identified above. 6.6.3.6 Drawings for the Fiber Installation For each DoDIN service installation, the Contractor shall submit as-built drawings to the Government. The as-built drawings shall show final configurations of the installation. Cable information (straight line diagrams, type of fiber, type of cable, date of manufacture, date of installation, fiber burial depth, cable/fiber identifier(s), and cable lengths) Notation of all deviations from specification (e.g., depth) Facilities (hut/central office) locations Origin and destination of each fiber (originating/terminating facility) Bi-directional OTDR traces of each fiber span Maps of any dissimilar fiber types within a span Locations of all optical events (e.g., splices, connection points) on the fiber Information that maintains manhole progression for each route that correlates optical distances (obtained via the OTDR) to physical landmarks such as manholes, buildings, bridges, etc. Locations of maintenance slack coils to facilitate response to maintenance requirements

The Contractor shall provide as-built drawings for the Government SDN locations showing their additions and/or changes. The Contractor shall provide as-built drawings for the Contractor-owned facilities (e.g., huts) showing DoDIN fiber and equipment. The required information for Contractor-owned facilities shall include but not be limited to cross-connects, floor space depicting Government racks, rack elevation view, floor loading requirements, and ducting. The overall system availability shall be 99.9% calculated monthly. The Contractor will continue to provide O&M support for amplifiers, regenerators, and terminal equipment. As part of the Maintenance Plan, the Contractor shall provide a process, subject to Government approval, to notify the Government via a web based tool, telephone, FAX, etc. within 10 minutes of the time the fiber failure is discovered. 6.8 OLA MAINTENANCE The Contractor shall provide maintenance of the OLA equipment in Contractor facilities for the life of the contract. The Contractor's Maintenance Plan shall outline its plan to provide two (2) types of maintenance support; Corrective and Preventative. In addition, the plan shall include a section on spare equipment management, where the Contractor shall describe how much spare equipment will be required and managed for maintenance purposes based on, but not limited to, the equipment manufacturer's failure rate Mean Time Between Failures (MTBF), the response and repair times, and the Contractor's field experience. The Government will provide the spares as GFE. Corrective and Preventative maintenance requirements are described as follows: Corrective maintenance ­ The OLA equipment located at the Contractor facilities will be managed and controlled by the Government. The Contractor shall have no active or passive monitoring capability of the equipment. Therefore, the Government, through the Global NetOps Support Center (GNSC), will notify the Contractor of corrective maintenance action needed. The Contractor shall maintain and repair equipment during the life of the contract by providing support 24 hours per day, 7 days per week, and 365 days per year. The Contractor shall respond to equipment failures after notification by the GNSC in accordance with the schedule in Table 6.8. Upon completion, the Contractor shall provide a brief report to the GNSC describing the fault and the remedy taken for each event, both telephonically and electronically. Preventive maintenance ­ The Contractor shall outline in the Maintenance Plan how it will provide preventative maintenance of OLA equipment in accordance with the equipment vendor's specifications (i.e., MTBF). The Contractor shall notify the GNSC at least twenty-one (21) working days in advance of preventative maintenance and any potential down time of equipment.

Table 6.8 Response and Repair Time for OLA Equipment Failure Event Response Time1 Restore Time2 Co-location OLA 2 hours 8 hours Equipment 1 Indicates maximum Response time after notification by GNSC. 2 Indicates maximum Restore time. Restore time starts once personnel arrive on-site. 6.9 AUTHORIZED SERVICE INTERRUPTION (ASI) PROCEDURES When a scheduled service interruption cannot be avoided, the Contractor shall obtain the approval of the DISA Theater ASI Manager before initiating any scheduled outage. To obtain such approval, a written "DISA ASI Request Form" must be submitted via email to the appropriate DISA ASI Manager with a copy sent to that Watch Officer (WO). The Contractor is expected to always minimize the duration of requested down time to ensure that contracted services are available to the U.S. Government to the maximum extent possible. This is possible only through appropriate planning, preparation, and/or use of alternate or spare facilities whenever possible. When a service interruption is required, the Contractor shall comply with the following criteria to identify the type of circuit release request categorization that applies to the service maintenance or interruption request. ROUTINE: Routine service interruptions are for those conditions that do not meet the criteria of Demand, Urgent or Hazardous Condition (HAZCON) maintenance activities. The Contractor's service release request shall be submitted and identified as a "Routine" request at least 27 calendar days prior to the execution. All power ASI requests must be made 45 days prior to the execution date. All requests will include a primary and an alternate date requested; failure to do so may result in denial of the service interruption. Request for routine facility maintenance should be made at least 30 days prior to the execution date. URGENT: Urgent service interruptions are for those conditions that do not meet the criteria of a Routine, Demand or HAZCON maintenance activities. Urgent service interruptions are generally limited to imminent or significant operational directed actions. The Contractor shall immediately notify the appropriate ASI Manager as soon as it is known that there is a need for an urgent service interruption to allow for as much lead time as possible for coordination. The Contractor's service release request shall be submitted and identified as an "Urgent" Request inside of a 28-day period interruption timeframe. A justification statement to waive the 28-day notification must accompany the request if notice is submitted within 28 days of the execution date. All requests will include a primary and an alternate date requested; failure to do so may result in denial of the service interruption. The Service and Agency NOC in coordination with the appropriate ASI Manager will review the request and justification for approval. If disapproved, requests will be returned to the requestor and must be resubmitted following normal ASI procedures. DEMAND: Demand service interruptions are for those conditions that do not meet the criteria of a Routine, Urgent or HAZCON maintenance activities. Demand service interruptions are for those conditions that must be addressed as soon as possible to correct significant deficiencies on DoDIN facilities, networks, or system resources or correct a problem that could severely impact a customer or mission if not corrected. The Contractor shall make every reasonable attempt to notify the appropriate DISA ASI Manager immediately to maximize coordination arrangements for the service interruption. Demand maintenance must be completed as soon as possible but no longer than 72 hours from the date of the request. The ASI Branch will send a message, when requested and if time allows, to all concerned that this action

Attachment 1, PWS Page 16 of 28 Pages

will take place. After normal duty hours the SCO or WO will process the demand maintenance actions. Demand service interruptions are considered unscheduled incident reportable events. HAZCON: A HAZCON is a maintenance action that is expected to cause no service interruption or outage to customers or one where secondary or backup resources have been allocated. The Contractor shall submit and identify the service release request as a "HAZCON" and define it as either a ROUTINE/URGENT/DEMAND ASI based on the guidelines previously mentioned. NON-SERVICE AFFECTING: The Contractor shall submit and identify the service release request as a "Non-Service Affecting Request" at least 5 calendar days prior to the maintenance event for cases where the service maintenance action will only result in a loss of service(s) for 50 milliseconds or less for the Contractor to perform maintenance on a tertiary power source. All ASI Requests shall include, at minimum, the below information. (1) Contractor making request, name and phone number of representative responsible for managing circuit release; (2) Circuit servicing Contractor NOC with phone number that can be contacted 24 hours a day and 7 days a week; (3) Organization performing maintenance; (4) DITCO CSA and CCSD number of circuit for which the request is being submitted; (5) Location of maintenance action by city(s) and state(s), only, or the approximate proximity and compass direction thereof; (6) Primary Date and inclusive start and stop times in GMT/ZULU for the request, along with an alternate and/or multi-phased event request by date(s) and start and stop time(s); (7) Purpose for the request; (8) Impact of maintenance action (Outage, Switch Hits, etc.); (9) Statement of whether the Contractor requires access to a Government site; (10) Statement of whether the Contractor requires access to a Government facility to perform maintenance; (11) Statement indicating all equipment, parts, and/or supplies required to complete action are on-hand, or their expected delivery date; (12) Statement indicating that all avenues of bypass capability (e.g., alternate facilities, spare facilities, etc.) have been considered; (13) Estimated maximum recovery time to restore circuit; (14) Contractor ticket number to track maintenance action. If an ASI Request requires the Contractor to have escort access into a Government facility, the Contractor shall submit two ASI Requests using two separate e-mail messages. The first ASI Request shall identify the building number and the maintenance downtimes. The second ASI Request shall have all remaining fields completed. This purpose for the separation is to prevent unnecessary aggregation of sensitive information (ex., Government SDP detail) and dissemination in unclassified domains and media per the DISN Classification Guide. The respective DISA ASI Manager is the sole authority for approving Authorized Service Interruptions. Failure of the Contractor to obtain an approved ASI prior to initiating a scheduled outage will constitute an unauthorized outage. Service interruptions without prior notification and approval (unless justified as emergency action) will also constitute an unauthorized outage. Unscheduled outages are not in compliance with the contract. The Government reserves its right to seek credits and other consideration as set forth in the contract for any nonconformance to performance standards. The Government may also terminate any portion of this requirement that repeatedly fails to maintain the contracted level of service or if

Attachment 1, PWS Page 17 of 28 Pages

the Contractor repeatedly fails to comply with the ASI procedures. 6.9.1 ASI Approval/Disapproval The DISA ASI Managers will notify the Contractor of approval or disapproval and will attempt to establish a mutually agreeable primary and alternate maintenance date. The DISA ASI Managers will typically notify the Contractor within 7 calendar days regarding routine requests and between 1 to 3 calendar days for most other release request types. 6.9.2 Prior To and After ASI Completion For each approved ASI, the Contractor shall contact the appropriate DISA NOC 30 minutes prior to the scheduled outage (to obtain final clearance to proceed), upon implementation of the ASI, and immediately upon completion. The Contractor will also notify the appropriate DISA NOC of any significant unanticipated impacts/outages in order to update the associated trouble ticket. If the maintenance was not successfully completed, cancelled, rescheduled, or failed, the Contractor shall provide the reason to the DISA NOC, which will update the trouble ticket. The Contractor shall follow the ASI Request procedures to reschedule maintenance that was not successfully completed. All information required in the ASI Request will be complete and accurate upon submittal, to include the "Required ASI Documentation Checklist" when applicable. Use of a Contractor's automated system generated form is permissible as long as the form includes all information required to be in the ASI Request. 6.9.3 Escalation Procedures and Contacts The Contractor shall provide its escalation procedures and designated points of contact to the Government within 15 days after award. Subsequent changes to the Contractor's escalation procedures and contact information shall be provided to the Government within 24 hours of the change implementation. An upto-date version of the Contractor's escalation procedures and contacts shall be provided for each IPR. The procedures shall include a description of the circumstances under which issues shall be escalated with associated timelines. The Contractor escalation contacts shall be accessible on a 24x7 basis. All escalation procedures and contact information and coordination shall be at no additional cost to the Government. The Contractor shall provide a name and contact number for a designated Network Operations Manager and Tier II Engineer that must be available 24x7 and/or return a customer escalation call within 30 minutes. The Contractor shall have a 24x7 NOC that will guarantee access within ten minutes to a live technician who can perform the following tasks: ˇ ˇ ˇ Create trouble reports Provide basic troubleshooting support in a technically proficient manner Engage next level support within five minutes

The reason for removal will be fully documented in writing by the Contracting Officer. When and if such removal occurs, the contractor will within ten (10) working days, assign qualified personnel to any vacancy(ies) thus created. 12.1 Access to Government Sites The Government reserves the right to refuse at any time, without notice, access to Government sites. Unless the parties to this contract agree otherwise, all site diagrams, pictures, and any documentation of any sort associated with this project become the property of the U.S. Government and must be handled in accordance with all applicable security regulations and as directed by the cognizant Contracting Officer Representative. a. A clearance is not required for this contract. Contractor personnel will be escorted at all times when access to Government facilities is required. b. The contractor may be required to access Sensitive but Unclassified (SBU) and For Official Use Only (FOUO) information and data in order to perform the work necessary on this contract. c. All network central offices and switching and wire centers shall comply with GR-63-CORE, Network Equipment ­ Building System Requirements. The DoDIN will be considered critical infrastructure and therefore requires Critical Infrastructure and Protection controls to be used for protection of DoDIN components and resources. The Contractor shall provide all ballistics protection rating information for all Contractor sites containing Government related fiber and/or equipment. The Contractor shall provide Government security staff access to physical security monitoring information of appropriate Contractor facilities. At a minimum, the physical monitoring intrusion detection system shall provide the following: ˇ Alarms indicating potential unauthorized physical access to facilities

Attachment 1, PWS Page 24 of 28 Pages

ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ

Alarms indicating environmental thresholds have been exceeded (smoke/fire alarms, failed airconditioning, loss of power, etc.) Alarms indicating threatening water levels in all component equipment rooms subject to flooding Positive indication that the physical security monitoring system is in working order and a means to indicate tampering with any elements of the system Alarms shall be provided/relayed to the Government in a "near real time" manner

If steel cages for network infrastructure components are used at node sites the cages shall meet all of the requirements specified in the Fiber IA and Physical Security requirements in the FRS and shall provide the same physical monitoring information of the intrusion detection system as noted above.

12.4 Government Evaluation The Contractor shall make accessible to the Government all Contractor sites, including huts, facilities, and co-location sites, in order to establish initial security requirements compliance, Certification and Accreditation (C&A) compliance, and for routine audits to regularly assess security mechanisms. Regularly scheduled assessments shall include Contractor cooperation to validate security requirements compliance. The Contractor shall cooperate in support of evaluation procedures and all components supporting Government fiber. Specifically, for C&A, the Government will conduct a formal Security Test and Evaluation (ST&E) to determine the overall security of the network. This will include an evaluation of all accessible Contractor sites. The Contractor shall cooperate with the Government personnel and the Government's representatives, who plan, conduct, and report the Government testing. The Contractor shall support the Government testing as outlined in Government test plans. Contractor support of Government testing shall include: ˇ ˇ Government or its agent access to Contractor facilities, test points, test personnel, and all components used to support the network Government ability to review all Contractor documentation used to support the fiber

The Contractor shall resolve, within 30 days, problems resulting from the evaluation process including vulnerability assessments and security findings. Resolution shall include: ˇ ˇ ˇ Component technical changes Procedures for correcting security findings Providing assistance with follow-on security reports

13. Government Furnished Equipment (GFE) 13.1 General If any GFE is provided the Contractor shall receive, inspect for damage, inventory and track GFE at the Contractor's designated facility. The GFE will be delivered directly from the equipment manufacturer or a Government warehouse to the Contractor's facility. The Contractor shall mark equipment as GFE in accordance with the FAR. The Contractor shall have personnel and material handling equipment available at its designated facility to facilitate the receipt and inventory of the equipment. The Contractor shall

Attachment 1, PWS Page 25 of 28 Pages

be responsible and liable for Government property in their possession, unless otherwise provided by this contract. 13.2 Inventory Management The Contractor shall be responsible for the GFE inventory from Contractor receipt of GFE until released from accountability as directed by Contracting Officer. The Contractor shall establish and maintain a program for the use, maintenance, repair, protection, and preservation of Government property in accordance with sound industrial practice and the requirements of FAR 52.245-1. The Contractor shall maintain property accountability of GFE equipment in accordance with FAR 52.245-1. 13.3 Transfer of GFE The Government will transfer GFE to the Contractor via this contract and DD Form 1149. The Government and the Contractor shall conduct a joint inventory of GFE delivered to the Contractor's facility. All receipt documents must be included as part of the accountability record file (i.e., shipping documentation, packing list, and Bills of Lading). The Contractor shall manage and maintain GFE equipment under this contract and in accordance with Federal Acquisition Regulations and via DD Form 1149. 13.4 GFE Report of Discrepancy When the Contractor discovers a discrepancy or damage to any GFE, the Contractor shall immediately notify the Government of the loss or damage. The Contractor shall provide a Report of Discrepancy on the loss or damage within three working days to the Government and the Contractor will provide disposition instructions.

FIBER INFRASTRUCTURE

The DISN transport backbone is a physically diverse, secure high-speed transport network. It is described more specifically as follows:

1. A meshed switched optical network across North America, Europe, and Pacific Theaters.

2. A network consisting of Dense Wave Division Multiplexing (DWDM) Reconfigurable Optical Add/Drop Multiplexers (ROADMs) and Optical Line Amplifiers (OLAs).

3. A meshed switched optical network, which provides for multiple service options at the optical layer including wavelength services.

This section describes the functional specifications required for the optical fiber cable and other transmission that may be used in the DISN. Specifically, this section states the requirements for: ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ Fiber Service Delivery Point (FSDP) Fiber Optic Cable Outside Plant Facilities Network Management Information Assurance and Physical Security

1.1 1.1.1

Fiber Service Delivery Point (FSDP) and Fiber Span Definition of Fiber Service Delivery Point (FSDP)

A Fiber Service Delivery Point (FSDP) is defined as a point where dark fiber terminates at a fiber patch panel which is collocated (i.e. within the same building) with an active DoDIN network element (e.g. OLA or ROADM). Thus, FSDPs can be physically located at both Government buildings and 7

intermediate commercial facilities or "huts" [e.g. Controlled Environmental Vaults (CEVs) or Central Offices (COs)]. The FSDP for the fiber shall be a fiber optic patch panel with all fibers terminated (see Figure 1.1).

1.1.2

Definition of Span

A span is defined as a length of outside fiber optic cable (including connectors and/or splices) from one FSDP to an adjacent FSDP (see Figure 1.1) which does not contain any active network elements (e.g. OLAs or ROADMs) along the span.

1.1.3

Definition of Segment

A segment is defined as a length of outside fiber optic cable which originates at one Government Service Delivery Node (SDN) and terminates at another Government SDN. A segment is made up of one or more fiber spans (and thus contains two or more FSDPs).

1.2

Fiber Optic Cable

1.2.1

General Requirements

Fiber optic cable will be a mission critical, physical component of the DISN. The fiber shall be of high quality; robust and able to support a myriad of functions in order to meet the overall stringent performance requirements for the DISN. Hereafter, for the described fiber criteria, [R] denotes required and [D] denotes desired. 1.2.1.1 [R] The fiber shall meet the standards put forth in the following International Telecommunication Union Telecommunication Standardization Sector (ITU-T) G.652 (11/2009), G.654 (10/2012), G.655 (11/2009), and G.656 (07/2010) except where superseded by the following more specific requirements here within. These detailed requirements will be outlined in the following sections. [D] For new installations, it is desired that the fiber comply with ITU-T G.654.C (10/2012) specifications.

1.2.1.2

1.2.2 1.2.2.1 1.2.2.2 1.2.2.3

Fiber Count [R] Fiber Optic Cable strands (one pair) shall be provided between designated Government SDNs. [R] If a new access fiber cable installation is to be fusion spliced to a commercial vendor backbone fiber, then the new fiber cable shall consist of 24 fiber strands in a single duct. [R] If an entire fiber span (SDP to SDP) is to be a new installation, then that fiber cable shall consist of 24, 48, 96, or 192 fiber strands (depending on the requirements for the specific installation). [D] All new fiber installations shall also have an empty duct alongside the single duct to facilitate future growth. [R] These new ducts shall be a minimum 70 mm in diameter.

1.2.2.4 1.2.2.5

1.2.3

Fiber Performance

The fiber shall meet the following criteria listed below. These criteria are based on a single span of fiber (from FSDP to adjacent FSDP). See Figure 1.2 for performance criteria for a representative span.

9

1.2.3.1

[R] The fiber span attenuation per kilometer due to all impairments (i.e., splices, connectors, etc.) shall be less than 0.23 dB/Km at 1550nm and 0.25 dB/Km at 1625nm at fiber End of Life (EOL). [R] Regardless of fiber span length, the EOL total span attenuation shall be less than 1 dB from the initial/ Beginning of Life (BOL) value.

1.2.3.3

[R] For all currently installed fibers, the polarization mode dispersion (PMD) due to all impairments shall be less than or equal to 0.1 ps/km1/2 for any single fiber on the span when measured at 1550 nm. [R] For all new installations, the polarization mode dispersion (PMD) due to all impairments shall be less than or equal to 0.05 ps/km1/2 for any single fiber on the span when measured at 1550 nm. 10

1.2.3.4

1.2.3.5 1.2.3.6 1.2.3.7 1.2.3.8 1.2.3.9

[R] The chromatic dispersion measured at 1550 nm shall be >= 2.0 ps/km nm. [D] The chromatic dispersion measured at 1550 nm shall be >= 4.0 ps/km nm. [R] Installation of all fiber shall comply with ITU-T G.655 (11/2009), ITU-T K.25 (02/2000), ITU-T L.35 (10/1998), and Telcordia GR-20-CORE. [R] Any single reflectance event shall be less than -40 dB. [R] The connector reflectance at the FSDP shall be less than -50 dB.

1.2.3.10 [R] The connector/ splice insertion loss shall be less than 0.3 dB. 1.2.3.11 [R] For all new installations, the splice insertion loss shall be less than 0.2 dB. 1.2.3.12 [R] The connector shall tolerate a minimum of +33 dBm incident power. 1.2.3.13 [R] The fiber Optical Return Loss (ORL) shall be greater than 30 dB. 1.2.3.14 [R] For all currently installed fibers, the fiber age (i.e., from manufacture date) shall be less than 20 years old. 1.2.3.15 [R] The accumulated insertion losses within 20 km of an SDN shall be less than 1.0 dB.

1.2.4 1.2.4.1 1.2.4.2 1.2.4.3

Outside Plant [R] All optical fiber, optical fiber cable bundles, and optical fiber ribbons shall adhere to the requirements as specified in Telcordia GR-20-CORE. [R] All fiber cables shall also meet the requirements of ANSI/ICEA S-87-640-1992, "Standard for Fiber Optic Outside Plant Communications Cable". [R] The Contractor shall be responsible for all permits, easements, and rights of way, to include Host Nation agreements/approvals. All work shall be done in accordance with the requirements listed in the following sections unless superseded by the local Government regulations. [R] The Contractor shall provide optical fiber infrastructure using underground installation procedures per Section 1.2.7. [CR] If an underground installation is deemed cost prohibitive due to environmental constraints (e.g., rock, etc.), the Contractor shall provide optical fiber infrastructure using aerial installation procedures per Section 1.2.8 or underwater installation procedures per Section 1.2.9. [R] The fiber optic cable between any two SDNs shall be installed such that it produces less than 200 rad/sec of polarization drift [(dynamic change in State of Polarization (SOP)].

1.2.4.4 1.2.4.5

1.2.4.6

11

1.2.4.7 1.2.4.8

[R] The fiber optic cable between any two SDNs shall be installed such that it produces less than 1 dB of power fluctuation. [R] The fiber optic cable between any two SDNs shall be installed such that barring a cable cut, its performance shall not vary enough to degrade transmission. This implies that changes of environment (e.g., temperature, physical external forces, wind, etc.) shall not degrade the performance of the fiber.

1.2.5

Physical Path

This physical fiber path can consist of a path that is (1) currently part of a carrier's own fiber optic backbone network, (2) an access path, which extends from a carrier's fiber backbone to an SDN, or (3) an access path, which extends between two SDNs without the need to use a carrier's fiber backbone. Fiber optic cable shall be suitable for the environment in which it is installed and shall adhere to the requirements in the following sections unless superseded by the local Government regulations. 1.2.5.1 1.2.5.2 1.2.5.3 1.2.5.4 1.2.5.5 [R] The fiber path between any two points shall be the most direct path feasible. [R] As an option, the Contractor shall, at the Government's request, provide fiber between the two SDNs at a particular site(s). [R] No DISN fiber pair shall travel in the same physical path or through the same physical facilities as any other DISN fiber pair. [R] All SDNs shall have at least two access paths. [R] For all SDNs with greater than 2 fiber pairs coming to/ from it, the fiber pairs beyond the first and second may use the same access paths as the first two pairs, respectively (see Figure 1.3). [R]If a node is a CONUS Central Data Center (CDC), then the SDN must have a third fiber pair that traverses another diverse access path. [R] Where dark fiber is proposed for routes spanning a body of water, the Contractor shall utilize 2 separate tubes (within/on the structure) in order to satisfy physical diversity requirements. [R] DISN fiber paths shall retain a minimum separation of 50 meters from other DISN fiber paths, except where two access paths are within 50 meters of the base boundary, but it is desired they be as far apart as possible. [R] For any and all DISN fiber paths which cross over one another the Contractor shall provide a specific mitigation strategy on a case by case basis, if the Contractor cannot meet 12

1.2.5.6 1.2.5.7

Splicing and Miscellaneous Handling Requirements [R] The maximum total splice loss shall be less than or equal to 0.3 dB per splice. [R] All splicing shall be performed using a fusion-splicing technique. [R] Connectors shall only be present at equipment interface points at FSDPs.

1.2.7 1.2.7.1

Underground Installations [R] Direct-buried fiber is not acceptable; a conduit/duct shall protect the fiber. 13

-

1.2.7.2

[R] A fiber shall be buried at a minimum depth of 42 inches or below the frost line whichever is deeper. For areas where the fiber is not buried at a minimum of 42 inches the Contractor shall provide an explanation as to the reason for this deviation and any risk mitigation approaches used (e.g. fiber is encased in steel conduit). [R] During plowing or trenching of a facility, a warning tape shall be placed no less than 24 inches above the conduit and no less than 12 inches below grade. [R] A buried fiber cable shall have a locating wire or conductive shield. [R] For open trench and plowed construction, a warning tape shall be installed above the fiber pathway and permanently marked with a warning message advising that a fiber optic cable is below the tape. [R] Surface warning markers shall be installed every 1300 ft., as well as at road crossings and culverts. [R] For all fiber cable within a conduit, the cable may be without armor wrap, but shall be installed in conduit appropriate for the local conditions and necessary protection from electrical discharge and rodents.

1.2.8

Aerial Installations

Aerial fiber includes fiber along a bridge span. If aerial fiber is used, it shall adhere to the following requirements: 1.2.8.1 1.2.8.2 1.2.8.3 [R] Aerial fiber shall only be considered where buried conduit is neither available nor possible to construct. [R] Aerial fiber shall be encased in conduit on a physically secure structure. [R] Pole line fiber is acceptable only where no other means is available. This fiber cable shall be enclosed in a protective structure (i.e. one that minimizes impact of weather/environmental effects such as wind, rain, snow, ice, excessive sunlight, etc.) for every aerial installation. [R] Pole line fiber shall be, as a minimum, a dual armored cable. [R]Pole line fiber shall be attached to a support wire or stranded messenger cable, doublelashed at minimum. [R] The cable and all associated hardware shall meet local Government requirements for clearances over roads, driveways, freeways, rail lines, structures, waterways, or other areas. All installation practices shall include calculation of strand sag, down-guys, over-head guying, anchors, and related items. 14

1.2.8.4 1.2.8.5 1.2.8.6

1.2.9 1.2.9.1 1.2.9.2

Underwater Installation [R] Underwater and Marine cabling shall conform to International, National, State and Local laws, regulations and standards. [R] Underwater and marine cabling shall be armored and installed in such a manner and location (e.g. not a high threat area) to protect it against external aggression (e.g. anchors, fishing equipment, hooks, grapnels, coral, rocks, sharks, etc.) [R] In the event of an underwater/marine cable cut, the cable shall be repaired within 3 days.

1.3

Facilities

The following requirements pertain to all Contractor facilities (e.g., CEVs, COs, etc.), which include categories such as floor space, power, HVAC, environmental, and location concerns. 1.3.1 1.3.1.1 1.3.1.2 General Requirements [R] The Contractor shall provide secure shelters, spaces, or enclosures to house OLA and ROADM equipment along the fiber pathways between the sites. [R] The Contractor shall ensure their facilities (e.g. huts), provide adequate power, grounding, HVAC, back-up power, etc. to support new OLA and ROADM equipment.

1.3.2 1.3.2.1 1.3.2.2 1.3.2.3

Floor space [R] The Contractor shall ensure the reserved floor space can accommodate the following maximum dimensions for each rack: 27 in (w) x 84 in (h) x 32 in (d). [R] The Contractor shall reserve floor space to accommodate a minimum of 2 racks for OLAs. [R] The Contractor shall reserve floor space to accommodate a minimum of 6 racks for ROADM/ OTN Switch.

1.3.3 1.3.3.1

Power and HVAC [R] The Contractor shall ensure a minimum of two (2) 50 Amp breakers with 8 gauge cable from Bus A and B sources (in accordance with the NEC) are ready and available for each OLA rack. 15

1.3.3.2

[R] The Contractor shall ensure a minimum of six (6) 50 Amp breakers with 8 gauge cable from Bus A and B sources (in accordance with the NEC) are ready and available for each ROADM/OTN Switch equipment rack. [R] The Contractor shall provide Uninteruptible Power Supply (UPS) for all equipment. [R] The Contractor shall ensure that their facilities shall supply DISN equipment with a power availability of .99999 per site. [D] The Contractor shall ensure that their facilities shall supply DISN equipment with a power availability of .999999 per site. [R] The Contractor shall provide sufficient HVAC capacity within their facilities (e.g. huts) to accommodate equipment, which may dissipate up to 2.5 kilowatts of power per rack. Geographic Location/ Environment [R] The Contractor shall provide the GPS coordinates and street address location of all intermediate equipment facilities (e.g. huts). [R] The Contractor shall provide the as-built path and GPS coordinates for every 50 m of fiber path. [R] The spaces or enclosures furnished may be existing or new, and may be used jointly by the Government, the Contractor, and others. See Section 1.5.4 Facility Security for further requirements. [R] If installed in an outdoor enclosure, the enclosure shall be hardened to protect against access and vandalism. If installed in an area adjacent to right-of-way for vehicular traffic (such as roadways, freeways, waterways, or rail lines), the enclosure shall meet the safety standards of the authority having jurisdiction over the right-of-way. [R] If an outdoor enclosure is used, the equipment installed shall be designed and certified for use in this application, with ratings for temperature and humidity changes for the area in question, plus a safety margin of not less than +/- 10% of maximums or minimums historically encountered.

1.4.1.2 1.4.1.3

1.4.2 1.4.2.1 1.4.2.2

Contractor NOC to RNOSC Data Feeds [R] Data feeds shall be forwarded to the Government Regional Network Operations and Security Center (RNOSC). [R] This data feed shall comply with industry standard management protocols and/or data formats and shall properly interface with the DISN network management system at Government RNOSCs. Such industry standard protocols for data exchange include but are not limited to: CORBA, SNMP, TL1, J2EE, and XML. [R] The data feed between the fiber Contractor's management facility and each of the Government RNOSCs shall consist at a minimum of one T1 circuit. [R] The fiber Contractor shall consolidate the various data feeds and provide the Government, to the maximum extent possible, a single data feed containing facility and environmental type alarms. [R] The fiber Contractor shall also implement mechanisms to ensure delivery of its common facilities' alarms to the Government network management system. [R] The fiber Contractor shall allow the Government to install encryption devices in Contractor facilities (e.g. NOCs) in order to protect and secure the data.

1.5

Information Assurance and Physical Security

This section presents the functional requirements for Information Assurance (IA) within the fiber plant and for the commercial facilities that house Government equipment and/or fiber. Information Assurance requirements are required to be identified and included in the design, acquisition, installation, operation, upgrade, or replacement of all information technology (IT) dependent systems in accordance with Office of Management and Budget (OMB) Circular A-130 Appendix III, Department of Defense Directive 8500.1, and Department of Defense Instruction 8500.2.

* Indicates maximum repair time. Repair time starts once personnel arrive on-site.

18

1.5.1

IA Implementation and Compliance The goal of Information Assurance is not finite; it is a continual process to mitigate the risks associated with all devices and subsystems of the DISN, with minimal to no impact on the functionality and performance of the system and services provided. DISA recognizes that Government IA requirements are more stringent than those observed in the commercial sector.

1.5.1.1 1.5.1.2

[R] In cases where an IA feature is not currently available, Contractors shall present their plan to meet the particular requirement. [R]The plan shall be presented and approved prior to the formal security test and evaluation phase of the system certification and accreditation. When, a requirement is unable to be fulfilled, alternate measures to mitigate risk to the component shall be provided.

1.5.2

IA Goals and Guidance In accordance with procedures outlined in DoDI 8500.2, the DISN is a Mission Assurance Category I (MAC I) system. The information it handles is determined to be vital to the operational readiness or mission effectiveness of deployed and contingency forces in terms of both content and timeliness. The consequences of loss of integrity or availability of the DISN are unacceptable and could include the immediate and sustained loss of mission effectiveness. The DISN systems will require the most stringent protection measures. DoDI 8500.2 provides three IA control robustness levels that characterize Mission Category I systems. The robustness levels are Basic, Medium, and High.

1.5.2.1 1.5.2.2

[R] Accordingly, the DISN is characterized as a MAC I system and therefore shall meet robustness levels characterized as "High" for integrity and availability. [R] The IA controls for confidentiality are likewise characterized through the use of Basic, Medium and High robustness levels. The controls for confidentiality utilize the medium level of robustness as this is commensurate with the handling of Sensitive or Unclassified Not Cleared for Public Release traffic. [R] In addition to DoDD 8500.1, DoDI 8500.2, the general functional requirements for IA are derived from sources that include DoD Guidance, DoD policy, commercial standards and best practices, and the National Security Telecommunications and Information Systems Security Instruction 7003. Where a commercial best practice is in conflict with a requirement defined in this specification or other DoD guidance, the DoD requirement shall prevail.

1.5.2.3

19

1.5.3 1.5.3.1

Personnel Security [R] The Contractor shall support explicit security roles and responsibilities. These responsibilities are partially listed in this document and shall be further explained later documents including, but not limited to, the Security Systems Authorization Agreement (SSAA) and the Service Level Agreement (SLA). [R- DODI 8500.2 ­ Attachment 1 to Enclosure 4, control number PRRB-1] The Contractor shall provide and follow a set of rules that describe their security operations and clearly delineate security responsibilities and expected behavior of all personnel who have access. The rules shall include the consequences of inconsistent behavior or non-compliance. Signed acknowledgement of the rules is a condition of access. [R- DISAI 630-230-19, B.4.h; DOD 5200.1-R, 6-303.a] Contractor shall have protective and corrective countermeasures in place to deal with a security problem. [R- DODI 8500.2 - Attachment 4 to Enclosure 5, control number PEVC-1] A current sign-in procedure shall be in place to control visitor access to Government equipment. A detailed log of all visitors shall be maintained on site and shall be available to Government at all time. [R- DODI 8500.2 ­ Attachment 4 to Enclosure 4, control number PRTN-1] A program shall be implemented to ensure that upon arrival and periodically thereafter, all personnel receive training and familiarization to perform their assigned responsibilities, to include familiarization in their assigned roles in Incident Response, Configuration Management, Disaster Recovery, and Continuity of Operations Plan (COOP). [R- DODI 8500.2 ­ Attachment 4 to Enclosure 4, control number PRMP-2] Only authorized personnel shall perform maintenance on Government equipment. The process for determining authorization and the list of authorized maintenance personnel shall be documented.

1.5.4

Facility Security

The requirements listed below shall apply to all types of Contractor facilities that house Government equipment or fiber. If the following requirements violate local government ordinance, local ordinance prevails.

1.5.4.1

Shared Facilities

If the DISN fiber or equipment is in a Contractor area and is concealed within similar commercial equipment, then the following requirements apply: 20

1.5.4.1.1

[R- DODI 8500.2 - Attachment 4 to Enclosure 4, control number PEPF-2] Every physical access point (hut, etc.) shall be guarded or alarmed 24 X 7 X 365. Two (2) forms of identification shall be required to gain access to the facility (e.g. photo ID and key card, or a cipher lock and key card for unmanned sites.) All access points shall have the capability to be observed 24 X 7 X 365 (e.g., intrusion alarm). Physical intrusion alarms shall be centrally monitored with an automatic law enforcement response capability to alarms. [R- DODI 8500.2 ­ Attachment 1 to Enclosure 4, control number DCDS-1] All dedicated security devices provided by the Contractor (e.g. physical intrusion detection systems) shall be documented by the Contractor and approved by the Government. [R- Security Classification Guide] Equipment or facilities shall not be marked with any reference to the United States Government, United States Government Agencies (including the Department of Defense, United States Army, etc.), the DISN, or similar references. [R- DODI 8500.2 ­ Attachment 4 to Enclosure 4, control number ECAT-2] An automated, continuous on-line monitoring and audit trail creation capability shall be operating with the capability to immediately alert personnel of any unusual or inappropriate activity. The audit trail records shall be available for regular Government review for indications of inappropriate or unusual activity. Suspected violations of security policies shall be available for Government investigation, analysis, and reporting. [R- DODI 8500.2 ­ Attachment 4 to Enclosure 4, control number ECAR-3] Events that will be audited include activities that might modify, bypass, or negate safeguards controlled by the system as well as actions that indicate the possible use of covert channel mechanisms. The audit trail records described above shall include:

Dedicated Facilities In some cases, the DISN fiber or equipment is separated from similar commercial equipment. In this case any of the following apply:

There are uncleared or unescorted personnel in a common area with the DISN equipment. The site already has secure areas (e.g. cages) within it. The facility cannot be secured to the requirements described in the previous section. The Government states that shared facilities is not an option at a particular facility.

In the dedicated facilities situation, then the following additional requirements apply:

1.5.4.2.2

[R- DOD 5200.1-R, Appendix G, Section B, Paragraph 5.e; DOD 5200.1-R, Appendix G, Section A, Paragraph 2.d] In secure facilities or rooms with windows in the space that are less than 18 feet above the ground, the windows shall be covered with materials that shall provide protection from forced entry which includes an Intrusion Detection System.

1.5.4.2.3

[R- DOD 5200.1-R, Appendix G, Section A, Paragraph 2.c] For secure facilities or rooms, all the hinge pins on all of the access doors shall be peened, brazed or spot-welded to prevent removal. [R- NSTISSI 7003 ANNEX B Paragraph 4,a, 1,d] A General Services Approved changeable combination padlock or some other similar access control device with Intrusion Detection System shall secure all access to all DISN equipment. [R] At the option of the vendor, all of the facility requirements specified in 1.5.4 can be applied to a dedicated portion of the facility. The dedicated portion of the facility shall house all of Government equipment and interfaces including the Intrusion Detection systems.

Fiber Protection If any of the following requirements violate local government ordinance then local ordinance prevails. [R- NSTISSI 7003, Section IV, Paragraph 5 and Paragraph 4, a,1,b] Transmission lines shall be protected adequately when they leave the facility and traverse an uncontrolled area. If Government fibers or cables are unmixed with commercial fibers, then they shall be installed in carriers constructed of electrical metallic tubing (EMT), ferrous conduit or pipe, rigid-sheet steel ducting, or some higher level of protective tube or pipe. An uncontrolled area is any area not within the secure facility, portion of the facility, or where the fiber is not protected by obscurity. Under no circumstances will this requirement lower any other requirements within this FRS. [R- NSTISSI 7003 ANNEX B Paragraph 4,a, 1,d] All access to the fiber (e.g., pull boxes, access manholes, etc.) shall be secured by a General Services Administration (GSA) approved changeable combination padlock. If GSA locks cannot be used, then a standard locking manhole cover shall be used. [R- DISN Security Classification Guide] Contractor provided fiber shall not be marked with any reference to the United States Government, United States Government Agencies (including the Department of Defense, United States Army, etc.), the DISN, or similar references.
