SUMMARY OF CHANGES 1. Foreword Section 4.3.2 MIL-HDBK-232A, RED/BLACK Engineering Installation Guidelines 20 Mar 1987 replaced MIL-HDBK-217F. 2. Foreword Section 4.3.3 MIL-STD-1678-4, Fiber Optic Cabling Systems, 20 May 2010 replaced MIL-HDBK-282 3. Foreword Section 4.3.15 MIL-STD 100G, 9 June 1997 replaced MIL-STD 100G, 9 SEP 1976 4. Chapter 1 Section 1.1.1 added clarification: QA inspection shall be conducted to ensure 90% compliance but must ensure no hazerdous conditions exisit. QA may be accomplished by the lead FE or independent team as deemed appropriate by the installation vendor. 5. Chapter 1 Section 1.2.1 added clarification: A detailed Telecommunications Services Implementation Plan (TSIP), with cautionary instructions for the field engineers, will suffice if the level of detail is sufficient to accomplish the assigned tasks. 6. Chapter 1 Section 1.2.7 removed: The exposed ends of dead cables or wire remaining shall be insulated with two layers of electrical tape or a heat shrink cap. 7. Chapter 1 Table C1.3.1 added: Cesium tubes, PolyVinyl Chloride-PVC and cabling, Brominated Flame-retardants, printed circuit boards, cabling, and connectors 8. Chapter 2 Section 2.4.1 added clarification: All 2-post equipment racks 7'-0" and taller shall be top supported by attachment to the site infrastructure, if existing site conditions allow. 9. Chapter 2 Section 2.4.10 added clarification: Where ever possible, 2 & 4-post Racks, cabinets, etc. shall be bolted to the true floor using approved floor anchors, stanchions, etc. 10. Chapter 2 section 2.4.16 added clarification: All 2 & 4post racks and cabinets shall be individually grounded to the equipment ground plane or ground bus. Racks and cabinets shall never be "daisy chained" to each other. All exceptions to this policy shall be addressed through the Release and Deployment Lead on a case by case basis 11. Chapter 2 section 2.5.11 added clarification: Insulation or heat shrink tubing must be placed on exposed threaded rods used to support frames, racks, etc... that may come into contact with wires or cables to protect the wires or cables from damage. 12. Chapter 2 Section 2.6.31 added clarification: Red and black fiber can share the same distribution vehicle as DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

long as both red and black data is not contained within the same multifiber cable. However, in TEMPEST facilities, Fiber carrying secure (RED) communication is to be encased in a metallic conduit or ducting and separated from BLACK communication by Protective Distribution Systems IAW NSTISSAM TEMPEST/2-95, RED/BLACK Installation Guidance. Red and black signal wires, optical fibers, power cables, processors and equipment shall be separated IAW NTISSAM 295, TEMPEST RED/BLACK installation Guidance, 12 Dec 1995, and amendments. Chapter 2 Section 2.7.39 deleted duplication of 2.7.36 Chapter 2 Section 2.7.41 renumbered as 2.7.40 and added clarification: Equipment cabinets are designed and configured, and their rack-mounted equipment is positioned to provide sufficient thermal cooling, natural air convection or forced air convection from internal fans to ensure the proper operation of the rack's electronic equipment in accordance with the specifications, installation and maintenance manuals of the electronic equipment. With the room's ambient temperature between 70 and 80 degrees Fahrenheit, operate all the rack's electrical and electronic equipment at full capacity for at least four hours. Then request network operations telnet into the devices to ensure equipment temperature is within a safe operating range before departing site. Chapter 3 Section 3.2.12 added clarification to use fire stopping at sites following fire stopping practices: Membrane penetration for cables, cable trays, conduits, pipes, tubes, wires and similar items to accommodate electrical, mechanical and communication systems that pass through a membrane of a floor or wall or floor/ceiling assembly constructed as a fire barrier shall be protected by a fire stop system at sites where fire stopping practices are currently followed. Chapter 3 Section 3.3.1 added clarification plenum rules followed only in plenum airspaces: Insulation of power cables installed in the ceiling plenum or below the raised floor must meet the requirements of NFPA-70. Communication cables installed in ceiling spaces and under raised floors shall be plenum rated or installed in a metallic conduit if installed in a plenum air space. Chapter 4 Section 4.4.1 corrected cable specifications: The maximum distance for unbroken Category 5 and Category 6 cables carrying Ethernet digital signals is 100 meters, unless otherwise specified in the BESEP, TSIP or EIP. BASIC INSTALLATION REQUIREMENTS

1. Purpose. This document outlines the general workmanship requirements for the installation of telecommunications and associated equipment by the Defense Information System Agency (DISA) or personnel to do installations on behalf of DISA. The intent of this document is to improve the quality of installation and workmanship practices, eliminating degradations to DISN telecommunications. It also prescribes procedures to maintain overall systems availability, ensure compatibility between electrical/electronic systems, and local ambient atmospheric and electromagnetic environments. Assuring human safety and welfare practices as they relate to workmanship and installation is also within the purview of this document. 2. Applicability. These are the minimum installation standards applicable to all installations of DISN electrical or electronic equipment, systems, and subsystems. The guidelines herein complement other specified technical standards and requirements that are necessary for the installation of the equipment, system or subsystem. Substandard installation practices can directly contribute to degraded equipment operations, electromagnetic interference (EMI) problems, Transient Electromagnetic Pulse Emanations Standard (TEMPEST) violations, poor power quality, grounding problems, and safety hazards at DISA DISN sites. 2.1 If conditions arise that, require deviation from the requirements described herein, a signed mutual agreement shall resolve differences between DISA NS6 and the installation team. 2.2 DISA reserves the right to revise this document for any reason, including but not limited to, conformity with standards declared by various agencies, utilization of advances in the state of technology, or integration of new products. This document provides a list of known specifications and standards whose use by Department of Defense (DoD) program offices, buying activities, and contractors and is mandated by Public Law or Government regulation.

C1 WORKING CONDITIONS, CABLE MINING AND HAZARDOUS MATERIAL/WASTE C1.1 General Requirements

C1.1.1 The Defense Information Systems Network (DISN) facility in which the installation is to occur, shall limit all communication concerning the implementation to DISA NS6. The implementations vendor shall be responsible for establishing a quality assurance (QA) process. The duties of the implementation vendor's QA inspector is to periodically inspect and evaluate the quality of the ongoing installation and enforce the implementation of the standards of this document. Sufficeint Recommendations for a successful QA/QC program may be found in paragraphs C4.3.20 ­ C4.3.23. QC inspection shall be conducted, at time of commissioning, to ensure 90% compliance but must ensure no hazerdous conditions exisit. QC duties may be performed by the lead FE or independent team as deemed appropriate by the implementation program manager. C1.1.2 All equipment is to be protected against any material falling onto or entering into the interior of the equipment during the installation. C1.1.3 The cutting, drilling, or filing of metallic material in rooms housing operational DOD communication/computer electrical or electronic equipment is prohibited unless absolutely Mission Essential and other equipment is placed in HAZCON. C1.1.4 Close all cable penetrations opened for the installation and/or removal of cabling temporarily at the end of each day during continuing work operations. C1.1.5 Opened cable penetrations require adequate protection for personnel and equipment where there is any danger of material falling to the floor below. C1.1.6 The Installation Teams are to maintain a clean environment. At the end of each shift, they are to clean the work area, clear walkways of debris or installation materials, and remove any trash from the facilities. C1.1.7 At the end of their shifts, the installers are to store their tools neatly in a secure area. Installers' tools are their responsibility to maintain and track. DISA or any other government agency is not responsible for tools or materials that are lost or stolen. DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 20

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C1.1.8 The Installation Team is to protect existing equipment and cable from damage during all work activities. C1.1.9 The tool used to crimp lugs is to have a ratchet mechanism that requires a full crimp before the tool can be removed from the connector. Only the correct size and type crimp die is to be used. C1.1.10 Wire wraps shall be made using the proper tool sized to the wire gauge. C1.1.11 A hoist is to be used to lift battery cells, equipment chassis or modules into place when total weight exceeds the "two-man carry" requirement. C1.1.12 When working under a raised floor, the area where floor tiles have been removed is to be cordoned off to prohibit the movement of all personnel not assigned to the installation team. Stringers supporting floor tiles are not to be removed at any time without prior approval from an O&M Site Representative. C1.1.13 After the installation or de-installation is completed, the site is to be cleaned and swept, all old cables, boxes and miscellaneous scrap removed, tie-wrap scraps removed from floor, and tools or scrap removed from the overhead auxiliary framing or cable rack. 1.2 CABLE MINING

C1.2.1 A detailed Method of Procedure (MOP) shall be prepared and approved before starting a cable removing or mining operation. A detailed Telecommunications Services Implementation Plan (TSIP), with cautionary instructions for the field engineers, will suffice if the level of detail is sufficient to accomplish the assigned tasks. C1.2.2 The leads associated with de-powered/defused AC circuits shall be removed from their assigned terminals at both ends and the wire mined or their wire ends insulated using wire nuts, electrical tape, or an approved boot. C1.2.3 Equipment designations and capacity stamping, associated with removed AC circuits, shall be removed. C1.2.4 Circuit identification cards inside of AC service cabinets shall be updated to reflect circuits removed or added. DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 21

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

C1.2.5 Raceway(s) remaining in the removal area shall be run and supported as specified by the NEC and in the job documentation, be securely fastened, and all unterminated ends closed. C1.2.6 Raceway and raceway supports associated with removed equipment shall be removed from its served point (far end) back to the distribution point, unless otherwise specified in the job documentation. C1.2.7 Open but unused knockouts in AC service cabinets, raceway junction boxes, etc., remaining in the removal area shall be closed. C1.2.8 Raceway junction boxes and fittings remaining in the removal area shall be equipped with covers. C1.2.9 Any AC wire nut connections remaining in the removal area shall be reconnected in an enclosed location, such as a raceway junction box. C1.2.10 When loosening cable or wire for removal (cutting securing stitches or removing cable clips), the Installation Team shall exercise caution and utilize the appropriate tools to ensure that adjacent cables, which may be live, are not damaged or cut. C1.2.11 The Installation Team shall remove wires/cables as far back as the job documentation specifies. C1.2.12 All applicable service interruption and/or degradation prevention and equipment protection precautions shall be adhered to during cable removal and mining operations. C1.2.13 All applicable safety precautions shall be adhered to during cable removal and mining operations. C1.2.14 Sharp objects shall not be used to separate cable bundles. C1.2.15 Wedges, lifting, or separating tools shall be nonmetallic and non-conductive. C1.2.16 When cable is being removed from cable rack, either horizontal or vertical, the Installation Team shall verify that DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 22

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
the cable rack is fastened to the building surface or a supporting structure before the stitching is removed. C1.2.17 During the mining operation, if it is observed that the ironwork, auxiliary framing or cable rack is becoming distorted, coming loose from its connecting hardware or displays unanticipated movement, the Installation Team shall immediately stop the work activity and notify the DISN Facility representative. C1.2.18 The Installation Team shall be equipped with adequate on site supplies to restore service interruptions caused by cable mining operations. C1.2.19 Under no circumstances shall a loop of cable or wire be inserted through the protective ring of a cable cutting tool to be cut. C1.2.20 All cables to be cut during a cable removal or mining operation shall have their ends hanging off the cable rack and all cuts shall be made a minimum of 18 inches below or to the side of the cable rack. C1.2.21 If there is a possibility of the cut portion of a cable striking working equipment when it is cut, the cable cutting activity shall be performed on the floor, or the appropriate equipment protection shall be installed to ensure that the cut cable ends do not strike working equipment. C1.2.22 To avoid the possibility of cutting loops of live cables hanging off cable racks, the potentially live cables shall be temporarily separated away from the cables to be cut. When possible, the cables shall be separated on the cable rack. If, due to the amount of cable on the cable rack, the cables cannot be separated on the cable rack, then the cables shall be temporarily supported with trunk straps (or equivalent) to the side of the cable rack away from the cable cutting activity. C1.2.23 If the job documentation or engineering specification does not specify the extent to which cables are to be removed from equipment frames or bays that are being removed, the Installation Team shall detail in the MOP the point on the horizontal cable rack where the cable will be cut. C1.2.24 If the job documentation does not specify the extent to which cables are to be removed or mined from vertical cable DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 23

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
racks, the Installation Team shall detail in the MOP where the cable will be cut, the cable hole(s) and the floor(s) where the cable removal or mining activity is being performed. C1.2.25 When removing cable on vertical runs of more than one floor, the stitching securing the cable shall not be removed for more than one floor at a time. C1.2.26 On vertical cable runs, cable(s) shall be cut from the floor above a cable hole allowing the free end to be identified before passing it through to the floor below. C1.2.27 All unused lengths of cord and cable clips associated with removed cables and remaining in the removal or mining area shall be removed from the cable racks. C1.2.28 The Installation Team shall remove, relocate, or add all end guards, end shields, framework details, units/equipment, equipment frames, equipment bays, cable and wire terminations, terminal blocks, etc., as specified in the job documentation. C1.2.29 All far end connections associated with removed units or equipment frames shall be removed. C1.3 HAZARDOUS MATERIAL/WASTE

C1.3.1 The DISN Facility shall adhere to the guidelines and procedures in their respective Hazardous Material/Waste Management documentation, and comply with federal, state, local, and provincial regulations. C1.3.2 The DISN Facility shall be responsible for identification and removal of hazardous waste prior to the equipment being removed and scrapped. C1.3.3 All hazardous waste shall be packaged per federal, state, local, and provincial regulations. C1.3.4 The DISN Facility shall be responsible for removal and transportation of the packaged hazardous waste from the site. C1.3.5 The Installation Team must contact the DISN Facility representative if the Installation Team becomes aware or suspects that hazardous material exists in the equipment being scrapped. C1.3.6 If the Installation Team uncovers hazardous material during the cable mining job (e.g., lead cable, arsenic cable, PCBs etc.) the work in that area shall be stopped immediately. The DISN Facility representative shall be contacted for disposition, and no work in that area shall continue until the DISN Facility has a resolution for the hazardous material identified

C2. C2.1 CHAPTER 2. IRONWORK, RACK and CABINET INSTALLATION

General Requirements

C2.1.1 This section covers the general requirements for the location, assembly and erection of cable and relay racks. C2.1.2 The Implementation Team shall ensure, as part of the evaluation of the installation, that all work has been done in accordance with implementation documentation or approved changes. C2.1.3 The location of auxiliary framing, cable racks, frames, relay racks and other equipment shall conform to the site drawings and specifications for each installation. Approved deviations shall be marked on the drawings. C2.1.4 All ironwork installation described in this section shall conform to the seismic requirements for zone 4,except where otherwise noted. C2.1.5 All fastening details, piece parts and other apparatus used in the assembly and installation of auxiliary framing, ladder racking, racks and cabinets shall be in accordance with manufacturer's specifications. C2.1.6 Cut ends of auxiliary framing, cable racks, bolts, etc., shall have sharp or jagged edges removed. Cut ends and damaged painted surfaces shall be repainted. C2.1.7 Auxiliary framing shall be uniform in length, at the correct height and properly located. C2.1.8 Splices shall be the through bolt type. C2.1.9 The end of the auxiliary framing should extend at least 3 inches beyond the last point of support. C2.1.10 All exposed ends of auxiliary framing shall be equipped with a rubber finishing caps. C2.1.11 When short sections of auxiliary framing are used below the regular framing, rubber finishing caps shall be installed on the exposed ends.

DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 27

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C2.1.12 There shall be a minimum 5-inch clearance between the ends of auxiliary framing and any building surface or apparatus (e.g., HVAC ducting). Any building surface or apparatus shall be installed with a minimum 5-inch clearance to the auxiliary framing. C2.1.13 Auxiliary framing shall be supported at approximately five feet intervals, not to exceed six feet and shall not extend more than 30 inches beyond the last support. The support shall be: From the ceiling using 5/8 inch threaded rods or from the floor using 2 inch pipe stanchions or wall supports using batten boards or Directly supported by rack/cabinet or other approved methods. C2.1.14 Pipe stanchion floor flange shall be fastened to the floor with a minimum of two 1/4-20 flat head machine screws and associated floor anchors. C2.1.15 Auxiliary framing should be installed in 6-foot sections unless otherwise specified. C2.1.16 Unsupported ends of auxiliary framing, supporting cable rack, ladder track, conduit, etc., shall not extend past the last point of support more than 2 feet 6 inches. C2.1.17 When a square tube floor stanchion system is used, it shall be installed in accordance with instructions given in the detailed specifications. C2.1.18 Stiffening clips shall be installed on no more than 2foot centers between auxiliary framing supports. C2.1.19 Stiffening clips may be omitted at locations where an earthquake brace, cable rack, or other clipped fastening of 1/2 inch or larger is located. C2.1.20 Cable racks supported directly by auxiliary framing shall be attached with J-bolts or C-Clip kits at each support. C2.1.21 Auxiliary framing supported conduit shall not be extended to wall-mounted switches, lights, outlets, etc. Approved flexible conduit or cable shall be utilized for this application.

DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 28

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C2.2 Cable Ladder Racks

C2.2.1 Where cable ladder racks are directly attached to auxiliary framing, both stringers shall be bolted to the framing at each end of a run. At intermediate points, only one J-bolt is required at each auxiliary framing intersection. The J-bolts shall be staggered so that adjacent fastenings along the rack can be made on opposite sides of the rack. When short pairs of auxiliary framing are used to support the cable ladder rack extending beyond regular framing, or are used for the support of a frame, two J-bolts or spanner clips shall be used per auxiliary frame support. C2.2.2 Cable ladder racks shall be located as specified on job drawings. C2.2.3 Space between ends of cable ladder rack stringer shall not exceed 5/8 inch at splices. C2.2.4 Only one cable ladder rack splice is permitted between any pair of supports and spliced sections are not permitted to extend beyond the last support. C2.2.5 Cable ladder rack shall be supported at approximately 5 feet intervals, not to exceed 6 feet and shall not extend more than 30 inches beyond the last support. C2.2.6 There shall be a minimum 5-inch clearance between the ends of the cable rack and any building obstruction. C2.2.7 Where required, cable ladder rack pans shall be installed using the following guidelines: Pan shall be installed on all upper tier ladder rack systems to prevent cable sag. All junctions shall be overlapped a minimum of 3 inches. The bottom section of "pan" shall not extend more than three inches past the common cross member. Pan shall not extend past the end of the cable rack stringer or closing detail. Cable retaining horns on "panned" cable rack shall be installed on both sides of the cable rack on 18-24 inch centers. An overlapping arrangement of pans should be utilized to avoid cutting of pans. C2.2.8 Distance between cable ladder rack cross members shall not exceed 9 inches. Additional support shall be provided as necessary to keep the cable from sagging.

DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 29

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C2.2.9 The ends of cable ladder rack sections shall be protected with rubber finishing caps or end closing bar. C2.2.10 Cable ladder racks shall not be supported by their cross members. C2.2.11 Vertical racks on walls or columns shall be supported at the floor and shall have intermediate support with a maximum spacing not to exceed 5 feet. C2.2.12 For horizontal cable runs, the cable ladder rack shall be placed with the cross members upward. A cable rack with solid bar-type stringers, smaller than 25 inches in width, may be inverted to gain necessary cabling heights due to fixed obstructions. Cable ladder racks with reinforced straps shall not be inverted. C2.2.13 All cable ladder sections shall be bonded together with a #6 stranded cable at every splice point. Only one bonding cable shall be required per splice section pair. C2.2.14 Implementation Team shall follow proper bonding procedures defined in the Grounding and Bonding section of this document. C2.3 Conduits

C2.3.1 Conduit shall be supported with material designed for the support of conduit, such as U-bolts, conduit clamps, conduit straps, etc. Hose clamps, cord, tie wraps and other similar material shall not be used to support conduit. C2.3.2 Rigid conduit and Electrical Metallic Tubing (EMT) shall be secured on a wall or ceiling every 10 feet and shall be supported within 3 feet of each outlet box, junction box, or cabinet. An outlet junction box or cabinet that is secured is considered a support. The use of EMT is permitted in applications where the EMT shall not be subject to physical damage. C2.3.3 Liquidtight flexible metal conduit shall be secured and fastened to a support within 12 inches on each side of each outlet box, junction box, cabinet or fitting. No support is required when Liquidtight flexible metal conduit is installed inside the base angle of frameworks. Three feet of unsupported Liquidtight flexible metal conduit from a fitting is acceptable DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 30

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
when flexibility of the equipment is necessary or when the Liquidtight flexible metal conduit serves lighting fixtures. Cord/tie wrap may be used to hold Liquidtight metal conduit in place within a frame (not for support). C2.3.4 Liquidtight flexible metal conduit shall not be used as a main fixed raceway for power conductors, except where flexibility of the raceway is required. C2.3.5 The total combined length of all Liquidtight flexible metal conduits from source to load shall be limited to 6 feet. C2.3.6 Conduit serving a junction box that does not contain a device and does not support fixtures shall be supported within 36 inches of the box, on two or more sides. If a junction box contains a device, conduit shall be supported within 18 inches of the box. C2.3.7 Conduits secured to other than a wall or ceiling shall be securely fastened at intervals of approximately 5 feet, not to exceed 6 feet maximum. Conduit shall not extend more than 30 inches beyond the last support. C2.3.8 Unused knockouts in boxes and cabinets and all unterminated conduit ends shall be closed. C2.3.9 Conduit shall be placed so as not to block future cabling, ladders and equipment. C2.3.10 Proper clearance from pipes, duct work or heat generating equipment shall be maintained to eliminate possible damage to cable. C2.3.11 Conduit shall be supported with material designed for support of conduit, such as conduit clamps, conduit straps, etc. Nylon cable ties, lacing cord or similar material shall not be used. C2.3.12 Insulated couplings shall not be installed in AC conduit or raceways. C2.3.13 Conduit fittings shall be tight.

DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 31

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C2.4 2-Post Equipment Racks and 4-Post Equipment Cabinets

C2.4.1 All 2-post equipment racks 7'-0" and taller shall be top supported by attachment to the site infrastructure, if existing site conditions allow. If a series of 2-post equipment racks (Equipment Bay Group) are tied together, infrastructure supports are required at each end of the group and one at the middle of the group. EBG's that exceed 20 feet must have infrastructure support every 8-10 feet. An equipment bay group or group of bays is defined as any number of individual equipment racks that are rigidly bolted or otherwise through-bolted together to form a structurally continuous unit of racks. C2.4.2 All 2-post racks shall be secured to the installation site "true floor" with minimum size 5/8" hardware at each corner, unless mounting a rack/cabinet to true floor through a raised floor using raised floor stanchions. In these cases 1/2" hardware shall be used to anchor stanchions to true floor and 5/8" hardware to secure racks/cabinets to stanchions. True floor is not the raised floor installed at many locations, but the floor that the raised floor is mounted to. C2.4.3 All 2 & 4-post bays 7'-0" or taller installed as an individual unit, not junctioned to any adjacent frames, shall have at least two points of support to the overhead superstructure. C2.4.4 All 2 & 4-post units 7-0" or taller shall be secured with 4 floor anchors. Top support should be utilized, unless specified in the detail specification. C2.4.5 All 2 & 4-post uprights of adjacent racks and cabinets shall be joined together per manufacturer's specifications and at the top and bottom to form a continuous lineup. C2.4.6 All 2 & 4-post racks and cabinets to be installed shall be measured from reference points as identified on the floor plan. C2.4.7 All 2 & 4-post Bays and cabinets shall be plumb and aligned to adjacent bays and cabinets to within ź inch. C2.4.8 All 2 & 4-post Bays and cabinets shall be level within 1/16 inch per foot. If shims are required, there shall be no more than a 1-inch shim stack. DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 32

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C2.4.9 If an embedded obstruction (e.g., reinforcing bar) is encountered during floor drilling, drill another hole at an alternate location. If relocating the hole is not possible, contact the PMO and Site POC. C2.4.10 Where ever possible, 2 & 4-post Racks, cabinets, etc. shall be bolted to the true floor using approved floor anchors, stanchions, etc. C2.4.11 End guards and guardrail closings are required on all bay uprights at each end of the lineup. C2.4.12 End panels shall be placed on exposed cabinet uprights not located adjacent to another cabinet. C2.4.13 Hinged doors or covers on cabinets shall not bind with adjacent covers or doors to such an extent that any cover or door cannot be readily opened without causing the adjacent cover or door to move. In addition, hinged doors shall not come in contact with any working equipment. C2.4.14 All 2 & 4-post Equipment racks or cabinets shall never be left unsupported. When equipment frames or cabinets are temporarily placed at a location, before being permanently secured, they shall be strapped to at least two locations (i.e. auxiliary framing, building column). C2.4.15 The following rack /cabinet clearances shall be maintained. ˇ ˇ ˇ Front ­ minimum 36" Rear ­ minimum 36" Sides/ends ­ minimum 24"

C2.4.16 All 2 & 4-post racks and cabinets shall be individually grounded to the equipment ground plane or ground bus. Racks and cabinets shall never be "daisy chained" to each other. All exceptions to this policy shall be addressed through the Release and Deployment Lead on a case by case basis. C2.4.17 Threaded Rods, bolts, nuts and screws used to secure parts or units shall be tight. The appropriate size bolt, rod, washer, nut, etc shall be used in all cases.

Page 33

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C2.4.18 Chrome rack screws shall not be used under any circumstance to mount/secure equipment. C2.4.19 The short chrome screws that come with ADC fiber management are acceptable to secure fiber management to equipment 2-post racks. C2.4.20 Stainless Steel bolts, nuts and washers shall be the preferred hardware to use when making DC power connections in rectifiers or in grounding scenarios where this type of hardware is required. C2.4.21 Implementation team shall cut the exposed end of a bolt or rod that extends into the equipment or wiring area, or presents a personnel hazard. ALL exposed ends shall be from nut flush to a maximum of three threads over flush. C2.4.22 Threaded rods shall be screwed into floor anchors or ceiling inserts at least a full seven turns. C2.4.23 Heat shrink or PVC type protectors shall be installed on all threaded rod that supports a second tier. C2.4.24 Bolts, screws or rods shall not be more than one thread under flush. C2.4.25 Both ends of bolts, screws or threaded rods free of sharp edges and burrs. shall be

C2.4.26 Self-locking nuts that have been loosened or removed shall not be reused. C2.4.27 Slotted Channel shall be at correct height, properly located and free of loose details. C2.4.28 Where Slotted Channel extends more than three inches beyond a clip or support, the Slotted Channel shall be equipped with finishing detail caps. C2.4.29 When additional Slotted Channel is placed below the regular framing, the ends shall be equipped with finishing detail caps. C2.4.30 There shall be a minimum 5-inch clearance between the ends of the unit-strut and any building obstruction. DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

C2.4.31 Slotted Channel sections shall have at least 2 supports unless otherwise specified. The supports shall be at intervals not to exceed 6 feet and shall not extend more than 30 inches beyond the last support. C2.5 Auxiliary Framing

C2.5.1 The location of auxiliary framing and other equipment is to conform with the particular floor plan and specifications for the installation as referred to in the installation drawings and Base Electronic System Engineering Plan (BESEP), Engineering Installation Plan or Telecommunication System Installation Plan (TSIP). C2.5.2 All auxiliary framing cut will have all sharp edges filed off and/or painted at the time of installation. The paint is to be of the color and type (enamel, oil base etc.) consistent with the existing or adjacent surfaces. C2.5.3 All materials (bolts, screws, threaded rods, framework, etc.) shall be secure and have no sharp edges or burrs. C2.5.4 The threads of bolts, cap screws, machine screws, threaded rods and similar threaded parts are to extend at least two threads beyond the final thread of the fastening device, i.e. nut or threaded hole, except in the case of cap-nuts and self-locking nuts. C2.5.5 The threaded part is to protrude no more than an amount equal to the diameter of the bolt, screw or rod. C2.5.6 Threaded rods shall be screwed into floor or ceiling inserts at least seven full turns. C2.5.7 All masonry or other types of anchor hardware shall be of the rating, size, material and type prescribed in the installation plan. C2.5.8 Holes that were drilled into concrete floors, walls, or ceilings and not used shall be filled with a masonry patch. C2.5.9 Auxiliary framing bars used for support purposes shall be uniform, level, properly positioned, and properly supported. C2.5.10 All fastening details, piece parts, and other apparatus used in the assembly of auxiliary framing shall be assembled in DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 35

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
accordance with the manufacturer's specifications as specified in the installation plan. C2.5.11 Insulation or heat shrink tubing must be placed on exposed threaded rods used to support frames, racks, etc. that may come into contact with wires or cables to protect the wires or cables from damage. C2.5.12 The ends of all auxiliary framing must be finished with the appropriate end caps. C2.5.13 Unless otherwise specified by the installation plan, auxiliary framing is to be supported in intervals of approximately 5 feet (152 cm) to a maximum of 6 feet (183 cm) on center. Each length of auxiliary framing is to have at least two (2) support points. C2.5.14 Auxiliary framing must not block or obstruct cable paths and openings, light fixtures, conduits or other similar equipment units. C2.5.15 Auxiliary framing is not to extend more than 30 inches (76 cm) past the last support. C2.5.16 Auxiliary framing splices shall be staggered whenever possible. C2.5.17 When splicing auxiliary framing, sections shall be a minimum of 36 inches (91 cm) in length. C2.5.18 When an auxiliary framing member is cut, it is to be cut squarely. The cuts must be positioned in such a way to allow for future expansion placement of a splice. C2.6 Cable Racks and Trays

The locations of cable racks and other equipment are to conform to the floor plan and specifications for the installation as referred to in the installation plan. Cable raceways shall meet or exceed the criteria listed in the installation plan or the minimum recommended specifications set forth below. C2.6.1 Raceways shall comply with all applicable Articles in the current National Electrical Code (NEC), NFPA-70. C2.6.2 Fill for all raceways shall not exceed manufacturers' maximum recommended allowance. DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 36

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

C2.6.3 A minimum of two inches of separation shall be maintained between metallic signal and control cables, and power cables regardless of whether they are parallel or perpendicular to each other. The preferred method is to fully enclose the electrical power cable in a conduit or ducting fabricated from a metal that shall provide sufficient electrical and magnetic shielding at frequencies below a kilohertz, such as galvanized steel. For low voltage signal cables, a minimum of 5-inches must be maintained from any fluorescent lighting fixtures and any power lines over 2-KVA. A distance of 24-inches must be maintained from any power lines over 5-KVA. Metallic signal cables shall be routed away from all possible sources of EMI; therefore, large motors, generators, induction heaters, arc­welders, radio, microwave or radar sources. Refer to MIL-HDBK-420, Volume 1, Sections 8.6 and 8.8, and Volume 2 Section 1.8. C2.6.4 In the effort of shielding electrical and magnetic fields from emanating from power lines, only ferrous metallic conduits, raceways, or ducts shall be used as raceways for the distribution of AC or DC power lines in DISN facilities. C2.6.5 All unused knockouts of wire-ways, electrical boxes and cabinets shall be closed or covered to prevent the entry of foreign objects into their interior. C2.6.6 Wire closets or distribution frames must be located away from sources of electromagnetic interference (EMI) such as transformers, motors, x-rays, induction heaters, arc welders, radio, and radar. Radiated emissions may not exceed 3 volts/meter across the frequency spectrum. C2.6.7 Wire closets and distribution frames may not be in an area susceptible to flooding. located

C2.6.8 Atmospheric conditions at the location of the wire closets or distribution frame shall always be maintained at 64° to 75°F (17° to 24°C), 30% to 55% humidity, positive pressure. C2.6.9 Lighting at wire closets of distribution frames should be at least a 50-foot candle measured at 36 inches above floor level. C2.6.10 In multiple floor facilities, wire closets shall be stacked vertically above each other with a minimum of three 4inch sleeves (a stub of conduit through the floor). C2.6.12 All conduits routing power cable must be galvanized or zinc plated steel and at least ž inch in diameter. C2.6.13 All conduits shall be installed in accordance with engineering specifications and drawings called out in the installation plan. In cases where a conduit run exceeds 133 feet (40 meters) the conduit is to be grounded at least every 100 feet (30 meters) with shall two AWG stranded copper wire. C2.6.17 A Metallic conduit terminated to an equipment rack is for the routing of power cables unless otherwise specified by the installation plan. C2.6.19 The total amount of cables in a conduit is not to exceed 40 percent of the cross-sectional capacity of the conduit. 6 8 (13.3 mm2) (8.4 mm2) 4 M) 2.4 M) Table C2.7.1 C2.7.18 Equipment frames shall be individually grounded to the equipotential plane or signal ground bus, and not grounded in series or "daisy chained" with other equipment frames. C2.7.19 The bare metal surfaces of equipments, frames, supporting structures, power and grounding systems that are bonded together must shows no signs of galvanic corrosion. A neutral metal shall be used to reduce the effects of galvanic corrosion. Metal surfaces of equipment, frames, supporting structures, power and grounding systems that are bonded together shall be galvanically compatible. Alternatively, they may be coated with a neutral material to reduce the effects of galvanic corrosion. Corrosive action between metals of different groups shall increase when the metallic bond is exposed to saltwater, saltwater spray, rain, or other liquids. The Galvanic Corrosion Guide Table is arranged starting with the most active (anodic) metal, magnesium, in the upper-left hand corner; and the least active (cathodic) metal, gold, in the lower-right hand corner. In addition, metals listed in the table are arranged in order of their galvanic compatibility with each other. Generally, the closer one metal is to another the lower the galvanic corrosion effects shall be, conversely, the further one metal is from another, the greater the galvanic corrosion effects shall be. In a galvanic couple, the metal higher in the series (towards the upper-left hand corner) are anode, and shall corrode preferentially in the environment. Metals widely separated in the table must be protected if they shall be joined together. This can be accomplished through metallic plating, applying a watertight sealant or paint to the surfaces of the bonding metals to reduce the flow of electrical current between the two metals. C2.7.20 All corrosion by-products, such as oxides, sulfides, sulfates, and other corrosion by-products shall be removed from the bonding material. C2.7.21 All nonconductive material must be removed from the bonding material, such as paints, other organic finishes; anodize films, oxide and sulfide films, oil, grease and other petroleum products.

C2.7.22 All solid matter which would interfere with the establishment of a low resistance path across the bond interface or which forms a wedge or barrier to keep the bond area open to the entrance of corrosive materials or agents must be removed. C2.7.23 Solid materials include dust, dirt, sand, metal filings, and corrosion by-products. C2.7.24 Mating bonding surfaces shall be clean and polished to a bright metal finish. C2.7.25 The bond surfaces shall be kept free of moisture before assembly. C2.7.26 The bond is to be assembled and sealed, if required, within two hours of its cleaning. Acceptable sealants are paint, silicone rubber, grease, and polysulfates. C2.7.27 Assemble bolted bonds for cable and strapping to a bus bar. The load distribution washers shall be positioned directly underneath the bolt head or nut that is next to the primary member. Lock-washers may be placed between the nut and any load distribution washers. Toothed lock washers are not to be placed between the primary bonded members but may be used as illustrated for interior locations where the bond is not exposed to moisture and where electrochemically compatible metals for the washer and bond members are utilized. C2.7.28 The proper bonding methods to a circular conductor such as wire and conduit are illustrated in Figures C2.7.3, C2.7.4 and C2.7.5. C2.9.15 Ducts and raceways shall be supported at least every 5 feet (1.5 meters) and within 2 feet (61 cm) of each end. C2.9.16 All ducts and raceways shall be installed plumb or level, except when changing elevations with 45-degree elbows. C2.9.17 All duct and raceway fittings shall be assembled properly, per IAW manufacturer's instructions or as specified by the engineering drawings and INSTALLATION PLAN. C2.9.18 The edges of wire access cutouts in ducts and raceways shall be covered with plastic grommet or other suitable protective material. C2.9.19 Ducting and raceways shall be made electrically continuous by bonding together all sections and covers. Associated brackets or hangers shall be electrically bonded to the ducting or raceway. Ducting and raceway shall be electrically bonded to the equipment frames that they feed through physically mating or by wide, flexible solid metallic bond straps. C2.9.20 Ducting and raceways shall be bonded to the facility ground system with copper cable conforming to the 2000cmil per foot (1X10-6 M2 per 30 cm) criteria. The bonding resistance between the ducting/raceway and the facility ground system is not to exceed five milli-ohms and is to be grounded not more than 2 feet (61 centimeters) from each end and every 50 feet (15 meters) along the length of the run. Ducts containing AC power wiring must be connected to the protective ground in the AC distribution panel. C2.9.21 Ducts or raceways must be squarely cut and deburred. The cuts shall be positioned to allow for future expansion and for the installation of a coupling fitting. Wire may not exit through the end cap of a duct or raceway unless the duct cannot be physically extended further in that direction. C2.9.22 Fiber ducts must be supported at least every 5 feet (1.5 meters) and within 2 feet (61 cm) of each end. The end of a fiber duct must be secured where it enters a cabinet or extends to a rack. C2.9.23 All fiber ducts must be installed plumb or level, except when changing elevations with 45-degree elbows.

C2.9.25 Fiber carrying secure (RED) communication must be incased in metallic conduit or ducting. C3. CHAPTER 3. Requirements C3.1 Firestopping and Plenum Fire Prevention

General Requirements

C3.1.1 DISN facilities are of a TYPE-1 or TYPE-2 construction; therefore its walls, fire walls, structural elements, arches, floors and roofs are of approved noncombustible or limited combustible material. C3.2 Fire Stops

C3.2.1 Where cables, conduits etc. penetrate floors or fire walls, fires stops shall be provided and have ratings equal to the fire resistance rating of the partitions being penetrated. C3.2.2 Written certifications or specifications verify that materials used in a fire block are fire resistance in accordance with NFPA-251 testing. C3.2.3 Penetrations through floors are enclosed in a shaft designed as a fire barrier. C3.2.4 Where concrete, grout or mortar has been used to fill the annular space around cast iron copper, or steel piping or steel conduit or tubing, that penetrates one or more concrete or masonry fire resistance­rated assemblies, and the following also applies: C3.2.5 The nominal diameter of each penetrating item shall not exceed 6 in (15 cm). C3.2.6 The openings' size may not exceed 144 inch2 ( 92,909 mm2). C3.2.7 The thickness of the concrete, grout or mortar shall be the full thickness of the fire-stop assembly. C3.2.8 Maximum norminal diameter of the pentetrating itemn is less than 4 inches and does not exceed an aggregate of 100 square inches open in any 100 square foot of floor or wall area. C3.2.9 Where there is an item penetrating through a floor/ceiling or wall, use a sleeve to penetrate the floor or wall. The sleeve shall be securely set in the wall or floor/ceiling, and the space between the item and sleeve shall be filled with a material that complies with NFPA 251 such as concrete, grout or mortar. DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS Page 57

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C3.2.10 Insulation and covering material for penetrating item shall not pass through the wall or floor unless the insulation or covering is in complance with NFPA-251. C3.2.11 Unshielded coupling shall not be used to connect noncombustible piping to combustible piping. C3.2.12 Membrane penetration for cables, cable trays, conduits, pipes, tubes, wires and similar items to accomidate electrical, mechanical and communication systems that pass through a membrane of a floor or wall or floor/ceiling assembly constructed as a fire barrier shall be protected by a firestop system at sites. C3.2.13 Any steel electrical box not exceeding 16 square inches (10,300 mm2) in area shall be permitted where the aggregate area of the opening provided for the boxes does not exceed 100 square inches (64,520 mm2) in any 100 square foot wall area and where outlet boxes are installed on the on the opposite side of the walls shall be separated by the following means: C3.2.14 By a horizontal distance of not less than 24 inches. C3.2.15 By a solid fire-blocking in accordance with NFPA-1: Uniform Fire Code [UFC], 2009 C3.3 Plenum Cable.

C3.3.1 Insulation of allcables installed in the ceiling plenum or below the raised floor must meet the requirements of NFPA-70. Communication cables installed in ceiling spaces and under raised floors shall be plenum rated or installed in a metallic conduit if installed in a plenum air space. C3.3.2 Coaxial cables, telecommunication cables, optical fiber cables, wire and cables intended for powering signal processing equipment, including insulated ground wire installed in the plenum, shall have a maximum flame spread density less 1.52 meters. C3.3.3 Cables installed in ducts, plenums and other spaces used for environmental air shall be of types BLP, CATVP, CMP, OFNP, OFCP.

DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 58

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C3.3.4 Abandoned cable shall not be permitted to remain in spaces used for environmental air. C3.3.5 Type BLP, BLX, CATV, CATVP, CATVR, CMG, CMP, CMR, CMG, CMX, OFNP, OFNCP, OFNR, OFNR, OFCR, OFNG, OFCG, OFN or OFC communication cables may be installed under raised-floor plenums, in enclosed metallic raceways in telecommunication equipment areas that are occupied by personnel involved only in the operation and maintenance of the equipment. C3.3.6 Cables installed in vertical runs and penetrating more than one floor, or cables installed in vertical runs in a shaft, shall be type BLP, BLR, BMR, CATVP, CATVR, CMP, CMR, OFNP, OFCP, OFNR or OFCR. C4. C4.1 CHAPTER 4. Signal Cabling and Wire

General Requirements

C4.1.1 The maximum distance for unbroken Category 5 and Category 6 cables carrying Ethernet digital signals is 100 meters, unless otherwise specified in the BESEP, TSIP or EIP. C4.1.2 Cables and wires selected are rated for carrying at least twice the maximum planned RMS current load. The RMS voltage rating of the selected cables and wires shall be at least twice the maximum planned applied RMS voltage or 150 percent more than the planned applied peak voltage. C4.1.3 All cables and wire shall be of the specified type, color, and gauge as outlined in the installation plan, Cable/Wire Run List. C4.1.4 Cables and wires are secured every 18 inches (46cm). C4.1.5 All cables and wires shall be positioned, placed and supported according to the installation plan specifications. They shall be supported and secured at least every 18 inches (46 cm). C4.1.6 Cables are not to be dropped between rungs of the cable ladder rack unless specified by the installation plan. C4.1.7 All wires shall be dressed in such a manner as to avoid congestion and stress on terminations, and additionally to ensure accessibility and proper clearance between terminals. C4.1.8 Cables are not to be routed to obstruct access to terminals. C4.1.9 Care is to be taken when stripping wire so that the wire is not nicked or scraped. C4.1.10 Wires shall be stripped to the proper length for accommodating the connection being made in accordance with manufacturer's instructions or applicable standard. C4.1.11 All spare and unused wires for planned future installation shall be long enough to reach any future required termination point. Coil and store all cabling designated "future" so that they can be accessed when required. DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 60

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C4.1.12 All spare and unused cable pairs shall be terminated to ground and properly treated (dressed in heat shrink, cable sheath, or fiber tubing and properly secured to the cable, fan, or form). C4.1.13 The QA inspector is to verify through sampling inspection that all signal cables were tested in accordance with the testing section of the approved installation plan or in accordance with the test procedures and standards as directed by DISA NS6 for the selected cable type and applications. The inspector is to be cognizant of the cable types to be tested their applications and the types that shall be performed on the cables under test to verify the quality of the cable and the installation workmanship. The following is a list of standard cable tests: operational bandwidth, insulation breakdown voltage, insulation resistance, impedance, insertion loss, reflectometer, return loss, standing wave ratio, etc. C4.1.14 Upon request, the lead installer or assigned test personnel is to present the QA inspector with a test plan for the testing of the cables that were installed during the installation. The test plan is to include test procedures for each different type of cable installed and pass and fail test criteria. If the installer or tester does not have a test plan as described above contact DISA NS6. C4.1.15 The test personnel are to show the QA test equipment and accessories used in the performance of the cable testing. All the test equipment is to be in good working order and calibrated. C4.1.16 Test personnel, upon request, are to demonstrate to the QA inspector that they are proficient in the use of test instruments in the performance of all assigned cable test procedures in accordance with the test plan, installation. C4.1.17 All cable measurements shall be recorded on data sheets. In addition to the test data, the following information is to be listed on the data sheets: Type of measurement, type of cable, location of the cable's terminations, date of measurement, name of personnel performing the measurement, manufacturer, and model number of test instruments used in performing measurement. C4.1.18 The QA inspector shall randomly choose from the data sheet several cables that were previously measured and request that the test personnel repeat the measurements before the DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 61

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
inspector. The tester is to demonstrate a reasonably good degree of competence and proficiency in the test set-up and performance of the measurement. C4.1.19 All measurements requested by the QA inspector shall be within plus or minus 5% of their initial value listed on the data sheet. If the difference between the proof-measurement and the initial measurement is more than 10% or if the measurements are not within the specified limit, the inspector is to notify DISA NS6. C4.1.20 When possible, cables are to lie side by side on cable racks without crossing one another. Cables leaving a rack are to retain their respective positions in relation with each other. Cable runs shall be planned as much as possible so that cables leaving a newly installed rack are on the top layer of cables in the wire way and do not cross over one another when the path of one or more cables deviate. C4.1.21 Where power cables and signal cables are run parallel to each other for a length exceeding 10 meters, either the power or signal cables or both shall be contained within a raceway, conduit or ducting fabricated from a metal that provides sufficient electrical and magnetic shielding below 1-kilohertz (such as galvanized steel or zinc plated steel). Otherwise, it is recommended that they are physically separated by at least one meter or more to prevent the coupling of transients or EMI from the power line onto the signal line.

No separation distance is required when the data cables or the power cables are enclosed in metallic raceway or conduit. C4.1.27 All power cables shall be routed along the side of the equipment frame that is opposite to the control and signal cables. Generally, ground, control and signal lines are routed down the right side of an equipment cabinet/rack, and power lines are routed along the left side of an equipment cabinet/rack. C4.1.28 Cables are to leave the rack directly above or below the cabinet, rack, or frame that it terminates to. Cables are to leave the rack, flowing over the edge creating a "waterfall effect", with no excessive slack and not pulled tight. C4.1.29 All cables are to enter intermediate and main distribution frames from top or bottom not from side to side. C4.1.30 Cables serving the vertical side shall be routed to the left of the transverse arm near the terminal strip and kept forward of the spacer bar in order to avoid interference with cross connects. C4.1.31 For cables other than connecting cables, the cable butts shall be located level with the first fanning hole of the terminal block, 1 inch (25 mm) behind the terminal block-fanning strip. C4.1.32 Cables serving the horizontal side of the frame shall be routed to the flat side of the transverse arm and secured near the vertical upright. C4.1.33 Cables then cross over the arm, make a half turn, and are secured in the channel of the transverse arm. C4.1.34 For cables other than connecting cables, the cable butt is to be located 3 inches (76 mm) behind the terminal lockfanning strip.

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 64

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C4.1.35 Minimum bending radius is to be maintained for all cables as specified by the manufacturer. C4.1.36 The inside radius of a bend in a conduit shall be at least six times the internal diameter. When the conduit size is greater than 52 (2) trade size, the inside radius shall be at least 10 times the internal diameter of the conduit. C4.1.37 When the minimum bending radius is not specified, the following criteria shall be followed: five X diameter for paired cables, and 10 X diameter for coax, triax, twinax, helix and fiber optic. C4.1.38 No cabling or wiring is to be routed directly from one cabinet or rack to another. All cabling between cabinets is to be routed over the cable ladder or under the raised floor. C4.1.39 The overall shields of interior and exterior backbone cables shall be grounded at both ends or in accordance to the manufacturer's instructions. A cable's overall shield is to be directly bonded to a ground conductor IAW the manufacturer's guidelines. C4.2 Multi-conductor Cable Terminations

C4.2.1 In cases where cable butts are covered with heat shrinkable tubing, the shrinkable tubing is to extend from 1 inch (2.5 cm) above to 1 inch (2.5 cm) below the butt. Heat shrink is not to be used on cable butts within connector backshells unless specified by the Installlation plan. C4.2.2 Cable sheaths shall be butted where the conductors break off to be terminated to the equipment using heat shrink tubing or crimp-type butts. C4.2.3 There shall be no changes or modifications made to the DSX panel or any other equipment. C4.2.4 Cables that enter a Type 66, 89, or 110 terminal block, or similar type blocks shall be butted where they enter the block. All four-pair horizontal cables shall be terminated in an eight-position modular jack at the work area. C4.2.5 Only a minimum amount of slack in the length of a cable is to be permitted in a cable rack. The excess length of the cable is to accommodate the changing of cable's terminating connectors five times and to relieve the stresses associated DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 65

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
with movement of objects to which the cable is terminated to or fastens to. C4.2.6 All shielded cables and wires carrying signals of frequencies less than 30 kilohertz or of data rates of less than 30 KBPS shall be ground bonded at one end only unless specified by the equipment manufacture or installation drawing.. Typically, shielded cables and wires shall be grounded at the distribution frame or block termination. C4.2.7 Connectors' shells (covers) shall be installed IAW applicable manufacture instructions or standard. There shall be no excess slack of terminated conductors inside of connector backshells. Conductors shall be fanned inside the backshell. Spare conductors shall be trimmed to reach the furthest pin and neatly folded or coiled inside the backshell. The connector shall be assembled with the strain relief engaging the cable sheath. C4.2.8 Twisted pair cables carrying signals greater than 1 MHz or 1 MBPS shall be terminated to Type-110 distribution blocks, or termination blocks having stray capacitance and high conductive characteristics that are similar or better than the Type-110 block. Note that the Type-66 block electrical characteristics are substandard to those of the Type-110 block. C4.2.9 The insulation of cables and wires that are to pass through areas used for the circulation of air in a building, such as ducting, raised-floors and suspended ceilings, shall be plenum rated. This guideline is not to be waivered due to the high toxicity of the gases emitted by some burning plastics that are used in electrical insulation. C4.2.10 Modular connectors shall be the proper size and type for the cable being terminated (solid/stranded, gauge, diameter, oval/flat). Cables shall be the proper type for a modular connector. The connector is to be applied properly. The strain relief is to engage the cable sheath. The conductors shall be pushed completely into the connector so that the contacts fully engage the conductors. C4.3 Light Guide (Fiber Optic) Cabling

C4.3.1 Fiber optic cables shall be segregated from other types of cables and shall be either installed in separate cable raceways or in fiber management systems such as fiber ducting. DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 66

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C4.3.2 The telecommunications outlet box shall be capable of housing two terminated optical fibers as a minimum. The outlet box shall have the ability to secure the optical fiber cable and provide for a minimum fiber bend radius of 25 mm (1 in.). C4.3.3 Light guide cables conveying secure (TS/SCI) information or data shall be encased in a metallic conduit or a ducting system that can be secured or protected from undetected tampering. C4.3.4 Light guide cables shall be routed loose without restraints. Velcro cable straps may be used to secure these types of cable. C4.3.5 When it is necessary to secure a light guide cable, the cable is not to be fastened so tightly as to cause damage or deform the cable. Optical fiber cables should be designed to provide flexibility for mounting on walls, in racks, or on other types of distribution frames and standard mounting hardware. Nylon cable ties are not to be used for banding or securing fiber optic cables. It is recommended that light guide cabling be routed in plastic flex-tubing. C4.3.6 Fiber cables intended for horizontal or centralized cabling shall support a bend radius of 25 mm (1 in.) under noload conditions. C4.3.7 When not subject to a tensile load, inside plant cables shall support a bend radius of 10 times the cable outside diameter. C4.3.8 The inside plant cables shall support a bend radius 15 times the cable outside diameter when subject to tensile loading up to the cable's rated limit. C4.3.9 Light guided cables shall be installed with no kinks, surface damage or any other deformity. Fiber cables intended to be pulled through horizontal pathways during installation shall support a bend radius of 50 mm (2 in.) under a pull load of 222 N (50 lb/foot). C4.3.10 The maximum horizontal distance fiber cable is 90 meters independent of media type. C4.3.11 The maximum channel distance including equipment cords is 100 meters. DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 67

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C4.3.12 The maximum cabling distance in a data center not containing a horizontal distribution area is 300 meters for an optical fiber channel including equipment cords. C4.3.13 Slack in light guide cables are not to be stored unprotected in a rack. The excess cable must be coiled into a light guide cable storage device. C4.3.14 When running cables are equipped with optical connectors, the connectors shall be protected with a cover to prevent damage and contamination to the connector. C4.3.15 Fiber optic cables that pass through areas used for the circulation of air in a building, such as ducting, raised-floors and suspended ceilings, shall be plenum rated. This guideline may not be waived due to the high toxicity of the gases emitted by some burning plastics that are used in the fabrication of light guide cables. C4.3.16 A successful Quality Assurance (QA) prorgam may include sample testings of fiber optic cables in accordance with the testing section of the installation plan, in accordance with the test procedures and standards directed, or as directed by DISA NS6. The following is a list of standard fiber optic cable tests that may be conducted: attenuation, end-to-end attenuation, continuity, length, insertion loss, cable assembly link loss test, cable assembly return loss, and end-to-end return loss test. C4.3.17 The vendor's lead installer or assigned test personnel should be able to present their QA inspector with a test plan for the testing of the fiber optic cables that were installed during the installation. The test plan is to include test procedures for each different type of cable installed and pass and fail test criteria. If the installer or tester does not have a test plan as described above, contact DISA NS6 for direction. C4.3.18 The vendor's implementation personnel should be able to demonstrate the use of their test equipment and accessories in the performance of the cable tests to their QA inspector. All the test equipment is to be in good working order and calibrated. C4.3.19 Cable measurements should be recorded on data sheets. In addition to the test data, the following information is to be listed on the data sheets: Type of measurement, type of cable, DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 68

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
location of cable's terminations, date of measurement, name of personnel performing the measurement, manufacturer, and model number of test instruments used in performing measurements. C4.3.20 The QA inspector may randomly sample data sheets and compare results to the fiber optic cables that were previously measured and request that the test personnel repeat the measurements before the inspector. The tester is to demonstrate a reasonably good degree of competence and proficiency in the test set-up and performance of the measurement. C4.3.21 All measurements requested by the QA inspector should be within 5% of their initial value listed on the data sheet. If more than 10% of the measurements are not within the specified limit, the inspector should take steps to correct the issue to prevent problems in future installations. C4.3.22 Unless otherwise directed by the approved installation test plan or DISA NS6, outside plant fiber optical cable installations and carrier wave implementations shall be tested in accordance with the following test procedures: ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ TIA/EIA 455-50B Light Launch Conditions for Long-length Graded Index Optical Fiber Spectral Attenuation Measurements. TIA/EIA 526-7 Optical Power Loss Measurements of Installed Single mode Fiber Cable Plant. TIA/EIA 526-14-A Optical Power Loss Measurements of Installed Multimode Fiber Cable Plant.

C4.4 Optical Loss Testing

C4.4.1 Backbone, single and multimode links: ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ Link Attenuation (Att)(dB)= Cable Att(dB) + Connector Att(dB) + Splice Att(dB) Cable Att(dB) = Attenuation Coefficient(dB/Km) * Length(Km) Connector Att + number of connector pairs * connector loss (dB) Maximum allowable connector loss = 0.75dB Splice Att(dB) = number of splices * splice loss(dB) Maximum allowable splice loss = 0.3 (dB)

C4.4.3.3 A horizontal link in an open office-cabling network with a consolidation point may be tested using a fixed upper limit of 4.1 dB. C4.4.4 Centralized multimode link: C4.4.4.1 The acceptable link attenuation for a multimode centralized optical fiber cabling system is based on the maximum 300-meter distance. C4.4.4.2 The centralized link may be tested using an upper limit for attenuation of 3.3dB. This value is based on the loss of three connector pairs, one pair at the telecommunication outlet/connector, one pair at the consolidation point and one pair at the horizontal cross-connect plus 300 meters of optical fiber cable. C4.4.4.3 A horizontal link in and Open Office Cabling with a consolidation point may be tested using a fixed upper limit for attenuation of 4.1 dB. C4.4.5 OTDR testing: C4.4.5.1 Reflective events (connections) shall not exceed 0.75 dB. C4.4.5.2 Non-reflective events (splices) shall not exceed 0.3 dB. C4.4.6 Magnified end-face inspection. ˇ ˇ ˇ Fiber connectors shall be visually inspected for end face quality. Scratched, pitted or dirty connectors shall be diagnosed and corrected. Optical fiber splices shall not exceed a maximum optical attenuation of 0.3 dB and shall have a minimum return loss of 20 dB for multi mode, 26 dB for single mode.

C4.4.6.1 The installation workmanship and the operational performance of an inside fiber optic cable plant shall comply with the approved installation plan, engineering drawings and test plan. Its design and performance shall comply with the requirements of UFC-3-580-01 and ANSI S-83-596, unless otherwise directed. Report immediately to DISA NS6 if the installation plan does not meet the criteria for a DISN facility, or if any of its engineering drawings or performance tests are found to be below standard or insufficient in content to conduct a QA inspection in accordance with DOD standards from DISN facilities. C4.5 Straps: Nylon Cable Ties (Tie-wraps), Wax Lacing, and Velcro

C4.5.1 Nylon cable ties are not to be used for banding or securing fiber optic cables, power strips or equipment. Velcro straps should be used to manage fiber optic cables so that the cable is not strapped too tight or the insulation is not crushed. Wax string should be used on all DC & AC power cables or bundled coax. When using wax string (lacing) care should be used when knotting string to present a professional appearnce, such as all knots behind cable bundle. C4.5.2 Nylon cable ties may be used to secure cable and wire above and below raised access floors. They shall be free of sharp edges. The tail or exposed end is to be flush or extend no more than 1/64 inch (0.5 mm) beyond the tail head. C4.5.3 Specific tools (flush cut) designed to cut tails off nylon cable ties shall be used. Tension of the tie wrap gun is to be set correctly for each application. C4.5.4 Nylon cable ties shall be tensioned tightly enough to hold the wires securely together and/or properly positioned, but not so tightly or at such angles as to cause possible damage to the insulation of the wire or cable. C4.5.5 The nylon cable ties banded around wire and cable must be capable of being rotated with slight to moderate pressure applied with the thumb to the head of the tie. The wires or cables under and/or adjacent to the tie may not twist when rotating the tie. C4.5.6 The permanent use of nylon cable ties is permissible above or below raised access floors in installations. DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 72

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

C4.5.7 Welding cables used for DC power or grounding shall be protected when secured with nylon cable ties.
