C5. C5.1 CHAPTER 5. CONNECTORS

General Requirements

C5.1.1 Cables and wires shall be of a sufficient length at the area of a connector's termination to allow replacement of the connector at least five times. C5.2 Soldering Connections

C5.2.1 Soldering connections are to have concave fillets around the complete connection. The soldering connection is to have a good wetting characteristic, evidenced by smooth feathering of the fillet onto the connection elements, and the formation of a small angle of contact between the solder fillet and the elements being joined. C5.2.2 Only 63/37 rosin-core solder or 60/40 rosin-core solder is to be used for making soldered connections. C5.2.3 Only rosin based flux conforming to types R or RMA of MIL-F-14256 is to be used for making a soldered connection. The flux used in the solder (wicking) braid is to be type R or RMA. Rosin base flux conforming to Type RA of MIL-F-14256 shall be used for tinning component leads of sealed devices, solid bus wire, and terminals.

DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 74

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C5.2.4 Solder connections shall be free of the following defects: ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ Non-soldered connection Solder bridging Rosin flux connection Cold solder joints Solder connections with stress lines Connections of insufficient solder Connections of excessive solder Solder splatter, Pin-holes in the solder Pits in the connection exposing inner surface of connection Contaminated connections Non-wetting wherein basis metal is exposed Solder connection dull grainy and gray in appearance Solder silvers Overheated connections where solder is dull and chalking in appearance Measling of the solder Improperly cut wires Excessive wicking where the solder extends to the wire's insulation

C5.2.5 The soldering procedure for cup type terminals found in connectors must comply with the following procedures: C5.2.6 Place the connector in a holding fixture at approximately a 45 degree angle with the open side cup facing up. C5.2.7 Apply heat to the side of the cup until the flow temperature of the solder is reached. C5.2.8 Slowly feed the solder into the cup until the required amount is present. C5.2.9 If required, place insulation tubing on the wire and slide it back out of the way.

DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 75

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C5.2.10 Place the iron on the side of the cup near the bottom and heat until the solder is molten. Place the stripped and tinned wire in the cup, bottoming the wire in the cup. Maintain heat until it forms a good fillet to the cup and wire. Do not heat longer than necessary to form an acceptable connection since excessive heat can cause excessive wicking under insulation. Ensure wire does not move while the solder is solidifying. C5.2.11 The soldering procedure for turret-terminals is to be the following: ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ Tin the conductor of the wire with solder. The bend in the wire is to maintain contact with post. The curvature of the wrap is to extend no less than 180 degrees and not more than 270 degrees. There shall be no more than three conductors for each section of turret terminal. Apply the tinned iron tip to the connection at a point near the midpoint of the mechanical wrap, and heat to the flow temperature of the solder. Feed a sufficient amount of solder to form a heat bridge to the other side of the connection. First remove the solder source, then the iron.

ˇ ˇ

C5.2.12 The soldering procedure for bifurcated terminals is to be the following: ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ Tin the conductor of the wire with solder. The wire or component lead is to be dressed through the slot and wrapped to either post of the terminal. The wire or lead is to be wrapped to the terminal post a minimum of 180 degrees and a maximum of 270 degrees (1/2 to 3/4 turn). The wire or lead is to be wrapped on the terminal post to assure positive contact of the wire with at least two corners of the post. The wire or lead must also be in firm contact with the base of the terminal or the previously installed wire.

DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 76

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C5.2.13 The number of attachments is to be limited to three per terminal post and is to be maintained such that: ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ There shall be no overlapping of wraps and wires. Spacing between wires, and spacing between the wires and the terminal board or panel is a minimum consistent with the thickness of the wire insulation. The wraps are dressed in alternate directions. Apply the tinned iron tip to the connection at a point near the midpoint of the mechanical wrap, and heat to the flow temperature of the solder. Feed a sufficient amount of solder to form a heat bridge to the other side of the connection. First remove the solder source, then the iron.

C5.2.14 The soldering procedure for pierced or perforated terminals is to be the following: Tin the conductor of the wire with solder. For wiring to a single terminal, the wire is to pass through the eye and be wrapped around the terminal between 180 to 270 degrees (1/2 to 3/4 turn). ˇ If wires shall be attached to a group of terminals such as on transformers, certain relays, and rotary switches, the wires must be neatly arranged around the terminals in such a manner that they do not cross one another. ˇ Apply the tinned iron tip to the connection at a point near the midpoint of the mechanical wrap, and heat to the flow temperature of the solder. ˇ Feed a sufficient amount of solder to form a heat bridge to the other side of the connection. ˇ First remove the solder source, then the iron. ˇ There is to be no burned insulation. The maximum length of exposed conductor must be 1/16 inch (2 mm) when soldering to any pin or lug. C5.3 Coaxial Connections C5.3.1 Coaxial cable shall not be spliced. This includes inline splices, barrel connectors, etc. Damaged cables or cables not of sufficient length shall be replaced. C5.3.2 Only approved coaxial cable and connectors shall be used. ˇ ˇ

DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 77

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C5.3.3 Only approved coaxial cable connector crimping tools with registered dies shall be used. C5.3.4 Coax crimps shall be embossed with the vendor ID. C5.3.5 Pin height and continuity (for open and shorts) shall be verified on every installed coaxial connector. C5.3.6 There shall be no cracks or evidence of double crimps on the outer sleeve. C5.3.7 Crimps shall not extend onto the tang area. C5.3.8 The crimped outer sleeve shall exhibit six flat surfaces with no fins or excessive rounding at the 60-degree corner bends. C5.3.9 The Instalation Team shall ensure that all coaxial connectors are locked. C5.3.10 Connector must be the proper size and type for the cable. C5.3.11 Ferrules shall be crimped using the manufacturer's recommended tool as specified by the installation plan. C5.3.12 The ferrules shall be butted against the BNC connector body. Only one crimp is to be made. C5.3.13 The crimp must be hexagonal with no burrs, flanges or excessive rounding of the corners. C5.3.14 The coax-braided shield may not extend beyond the point where the ferrule and connector body meet. C5.3.15 The outer jacket of the coax cable must be under the ferrule. C5.3.16 Crimped center pins on BNC connectors shall be done using only the manufacturer's recommended tools as specified by the installation plan. The center pin is to be soldered to a solid center conductor. C5.3.17 Miniature coaxial/twinax cable is to be routed and supported to eliminate any strain on the terminated end of the miniature coaxial cable. DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 78

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

C5.3.18 The connector is to be of the proper size and type for the cable. It is to be assembled properly, using the proper tool(s). The strain relief (nut or ferrule) is to engage with the cable sheath. C5.4 Shield Connection

C5.4.1 The shields of shielded cables shall be cut, positioned and bonded to ground as specified in the job documentation. C5.4.2 Shielded cable and wire shall have the shield ground bonded at one end only. This bonding shall be at the equipment (originating) end unless the product design specifies otherwise. Exposed shields of shielded cable shall be protected with two half-lapped layers of electrical tape or heat shrinkable sleeving. C5.4.3 On shielded switchboard cable, the drain lead shall be protected by applying sleeving material. C5.5 Quick-Connect

C5.5.1 Only one wire shall be engaged in each terminal. C5.5.2 Only solder sleeve type splicing connectors shall be used for splicing individual leads. C5.5.3 Conductors shall not be placed on deformed terminals. C5.5.4 Previously terminated wire ends shall not be reterminated. Cut them off and use new ends. C5.5.5 Wire ends shall protrude 1/16 inch beyond edge of clipped terminal. C5.5.6 Wire ends shall clear adjacent metallic parts by 1/32 of an inch minimum. C5.5.7 Textile-insulated wire shall not be terminated in slotted beam terminals. Wire Wrapping C5.6.1 Wire wraps shall be made using the tool sized to the wire gauge. DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 79

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

C5.6.2 On terminals that are not square, #22-gauge wire shall have a minimum of five wraps and a maximum of seven wraps. C5.6.3 Overlapped turns are not to be counted in the number of turns of a connection. C5.6.4 Wire of gauges #28, 30 or 32 shall have one wrap of insulation in addition to the required number of wraps. C5.6.5 All connections not meeting the requirements shall be reskinned and reconnected. C5.6.6 Installation Team shall not solder #26 through #32-gauge wire. C5.6.7 Exposed un-insulated wire (shiner) shall not exceed 1/8 inch. C5.6.8 Clearance between connections and adjacent metalwork shall be 1/32 of an inch minimum. The wire end projection shall not violate the minimum clearance. C5.6.9 Clearances between adjacent connections shall be 1/64 of an inch minimum. The wire end projection shall not violate the minimum clearance. Wire wrap terminals on blocks, backplanes, etc. shall be straight and not bent. C5.6.10 Cable may be spliced using modular splicing apparatus. These splices shall be done in accordance with the manufacturer's specification. The Engineer will approve any use of these connectors. C5.6.11 The index strip shall have two wires in each slot. C5.6.12 Both halves of the connector body shall be fully latched. If not self-latching, or fitted with locking screws or securing clips, the two halves shall be secured on each end with 9-ply polyester twine, except when they need to remain readily available for rapid opening (e.g., for dial-to-dial conversion activity). C5.6.13 The cap shall be fully latched to the connector body and index strip.

DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 80

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C5.6.14 When connectors are placed on cable racks or pressed into adjacent cables they shall be covered with heat shrink tubing. C5.6.15 Cables fitted with connectors, but not connected, shall be secured with waxed fiber cord so that the cables shall not protrude into the wiring aisle behind the bay. C5.4 RJ-45 Connections

C5.7.1 Use the proper connector. Use CAT-5 connectors with CAT5 cable. Use CAT-6 connectors with CAT-6 cable. C5.7.2 When removing outer cable sheath do not nick individual wire sheaths. C5.7.3 Remove enough outer sheath to allow for easy manipulation of individual wires, normally 2" is more than adequate. C5.7.4 When dealing with CAT-6 cable, once the outer sheath has been removed, push the four pairs of wire toward the outer sheath to expose as much of the inner separation core as possible. CAT-5 cable does not have this inner core. C5.7.5 Cut the inner core as close as possible. C5.7.6 Separate the wire pairs and straighten out the twists. This shall allow easier manipulation of the wires. C5.7.7 Fan the wires out to the correct termination configuration. Press the wires between your thumb and first finger and wiggle the wire ends back and forth lightly to set the configuration. C5.7.8 Cut the excess wire length so that all connector wires are flush. If not all wires are flush when inserted into connector, there is a good chance the finished connector shall fail in testing. C5.7.9 When cable is inserted into RJ45 connector, there shall be between 1/4" and 5/16" of sheath inside connector. When connector is properly crimped, the sheath keeps the cable from moving around inside the connector. Cables that can move in the connector can cause cable failures, and shall not be used.

DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 81

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C5.7.10 All Ethernet cables shall be tested with approved Ethernet cable tester.

C5.8

BNC Connections

C5.8.1 Always use the correct connector for the cable that is to be installed. C5.8.2 Use correct tools to correctly prepare cable and terminate connectors. C5.8.3 Carefully remove outer cable protection sheath on multibundled cables, i.e. 6-pak, 12-pak, 24-pak, etc. Avoid cutting or nicking individual wire sheaths. C5.8.4 If nicking or cutting individual wire sheaths occur, Installation Team shall cut the entire bundle flush and start over. C5.8.5 Strip back outer sheath to a length that allows individual wires to easily flex into their termination point. An average for most installations is approximately 18" to 24". C5.8.6 Carefully trim off the outer sheath. Installation Team shall use either electrical tape or heat shrink over the outer sheath/individual wire bundle to provide a clean look. In this case clear heat shrink is not a requirement. C5.8.7 During the cable termination process, avoid wire bunching. This is caused when wires are not pre-measured and as DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 82

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
wires get terminated to closer connections, the excess wire starts bunching towards the opposite end of the cable. This makes dressing in the cables difficult and normally leaves a messy finished look. C5.8.8 Before stripping wires, take a few spare wires and use the sheath stripper on them to verify sheath stripper is making the proper depth cuts. C5.5 D SUB plugs, contacts connectors and housings (db-xx) D

C5.9.1 This section shall cover D SUB crimp type connections. SUB solder-type connections shall not be covered in this document at this time. C5.9.2 D SUB plug and socket contacts shall be barrel type crimp.

C5.9.3 D SUB contacts shall be US government approved under MILSPEC (Military Specification) requirements. Sockets and contacts that meet this requirement, AMP 205089, AMP 205090. C5.9.4 Crimping tool shall be ratchet type that must complete a full crimp ratchet before it releases. C5.9.5 Crimping tool shall complete a minimum 4-point crimp to a maximum 8-point crimp. C5.9.6 D SUB shells shall have metal plating and match the D SUB contacts for proper connectivity. C5.9.7 Connector covers shall be metal and meet US Government MIL-SPEC requirements. C5.9.8 Plastic D SUB connectors and covers, conversion connectors, etc. shall not be used on any cable. C5.9.9 Cables supplied by equipment manufacturers specifically made for the operation of their equipment are exempt at this time. C5.9.10 Adequate strain relief protection on cable exiting cover shall be used to minimize cable movement within the connector, which can cause cable failure.

DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 82

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
D SUB Connector Plug and Socket Installation C5.9.11 Under normal circumstances, Category 5 or 5E cable should be sufficient for most installations. C5.9.12 Install the correct size strain relief sleeve over the cable. C5.9.13 Remove approximately 1 ˝" of outer cable protection sheath. Avoid cutting or nicking individual wire sheaths. C5.9.14 Separate the color wire pairs. This shall make it easier to apply the D SUB plug and socket pins. C5.9.15 Strip approximately 1/16" to 1/8" from the end of each of the individual wire sheaths. Even though the crimping tool should break the sheath and make the wire-to pin connection when crimped, experience has taught us that this extra step greatly reduces connector fail rates. C5.9.16 Slide the D SUB plug (male pin) or socket (female pin) over the wire and push pin against wire as far as possible. Previously stripped wire end should end up in the pin part of the connector. C5.9.17 Slide the pin/wire into the crimp tool making sure the wire is fully seated into the pin. C5.9.18 Complete one ratchet crimp movement. Once ratchet full disengages, remove pin/wire from crimper and visually inspect crimp integrity. C5.9.19 Firmly hold on to the pin and moderately tug on the wire to verify connection is sound. C5.9.20 Once all D SUB plug or socket pins are crimped, installing into the connector can begin. C5.9.21 All D SUB connector pin inserts are numbered from 1 to XX, depending on the connector size. Follow whatever wiring pin out requirement based on the equipment termination requirement.

DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 83

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C5.9.22 Instalation Team should always use a pin insertion/extraction tool to insert or remove pins from connector. The insertion part of the tool prevents the wire from collapsing into to pin connector when it is pushed into the connector. The extraction part of the tool releases the connector pin from the connector without damaging the wire or connector pin. C5.9.23 Place the insertion tool over the connector pin sleeve and insert the connector pin with tool into the connector pin hole and push until there is a click. This means the connector pin is properly seated in the connector. Hold the connector and tug on the wire to verify connector is actually seated. C5.9.24 Place one half of the connector cover on the connector, slide the strain relief sleeve into place on the connector cover and manage the wires in the cover so there is no pinching or crimping of wires. C5.9.25 Place the other half of the cover on the connector and install securing hardware.

C5.10.1 All crimps or compression connections using the various types of commercial connectors shall be properly made with the number of crimps being determined by the supplying manufacturer's requirements pertaining to wire gauge, type of lug, and the crimp or compression tool used.

C5.10.2 Only connectors and splices with an electrical rating that exceeds the predicted current and voltage of a termination may be used. C5.10.3 Connectors shall be made of tin-plated copper with an insulated barrel, unless otherwise specified by the installation plan. C5.10.4 Wires shall be inserted so that they extend 1/16 inch (2 mm) past the barrel of the lug. C5.10.5 Space between wire insulation and the body of solderless connectors and power lugs shall be kept to a maximum of 1/16 inch (2 mm). Solid wire must not be nicked. Stranded wire may not have any strands cut off. C5.10.6 Crimps may not extend onto the tang area. C5.10.7 The number and sequence of crimps must be appropriate for the connector used. C5.10.8 The connector must agree with the wire size as follows for #10-22 AWG (5.27 - 0.63 mm2): Red Terminal Blue Terminal Yellow Terminal #22 - #18 AWG (0.63 - 0.82 mm2) #16 - #14 AWG (1.31 - 2.08 mm2) #12 - #10 AWG (3.31 - 5.27 mm2)

C5.11.1 All connections not meeting the requirements of this section shall be soldered. C5.11.2 When one connection on a terminal is soldered then all connections on that terminal shall be soldered. C5.11.3 There shall be no separations between turns of wire on the terminal. Wraps must begin at the bottom of the terminal. C5.11.4 Insulation shall be within 1/32 inch (1 mm) of the terminal, or a modified wrap. C5.11.5 20-24 AWG wires are to have minimum of five nonoverlapping turns. C5.11.6 26-AWG wires are to have a minimum of seven nonoverlapping turns. C5.11.7 28 & 30 AWG (0.08 - 0.05 mm2) wires are to have a minimum of seven non-overlapping turns plus a full turn of insulation. C5.11.8 The size of the wire may not exceed the capabilities of the terminals. C5.11.9 There shall not be wire-end projections. C5.11.10 No turns of any connection are to overlap the turns of any existing connection on the same terminal. There shall be no gap between multiple connections on the same terminal. C5.11.11 The end of a wire is not to be over-wrapped. C5.11.12 All wraps shall be made in the clockwise direction. C5.7 Optical Fiber Connectors C5.12.1 All connectors, adapters, and cable assemblies shall comply with the Interconnect SID and the Cable Run List of the installation plan. C5.12.2 The telecommunications outlet box shall be capable of housing two terminated optical fibers as a minimum, and provide for a minimum fiber bend radius of 25mm (1 in). C6. Drawings C6.1 CHAPTER 6. Equipment Designations, Labeling and

General Requirements

C6.1.1 It is the installer's responsibility to apply all equipment designations IAW the Defense Information Systems Network's Managed Element Naming Convention. C6.1.2 The top front of an equipment rack is to be labeled with the following information: ˇ ˇ ˇ The rack number and row number where the equipment cabinet is installed. The sequential number of the rack in respect to the adjacent equipment cabinets. The number of the circuit breaker and its breaker panel that the frame's power cable is terminated to must be clearly labeled on the front and rear side of the frame. Lettering shall be ž inch (19 mm) in size.

ˇ

C6.1.3 Labeling machines may be used in place of rubber stamps and ink, as long as the proper character size and color are adhered to. C6.2 Character Colors

C6.2.1 Black lettering on white background or individual white lettering are required on racks and cabinets. C6.2.2 Caution notices shall be in white or black on a red background. C6.2.3 Fuse ratings shall be in black on a yellow background. C6.2.4 Outlets that supply AC power shall be designated with the voltage and applicable circuit breaker designator in black on a white background on the front or side of the outlet.

C6.3 Equipment and Frame Labeling Requirements

C6.3.1 The purpose of this section is to provide a detailed, comprehensive and easy to follow instruction guide regarding standard labeling procedures for all technologies. This section will cover: ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ Label Size Label Type Label Color Ink Colors Label Information

C6.3.2 Additional labeling can be added to other equipment such as Ciena Transceiver and MUX/DEMUX shelves or adding a label that identifies the link that the Ciena gear is transporting C6.3.3 It has been determined that the best devices to use to generate and print labels are the Brady TLS series thermal labelers and the Brother P-Touch series labels that can hold 3/4" labels. C6.3.4 The standard Brady label is part number PTL-64-427 C6.3.5 The standard Brother P-Touch labels are all 3/4 " white back with either, Black, Red or Blue lettering, depending on application. C6.3.6 Labels at equipment ends shall be located as close to the connector end as possible without interfering with equipment or cable functionality. C6.3.7 Labels at the FDP (rear) shall be placed a minimum of 4 inches from connector so that labels are easier to read. C6.3.8 Labels at FDP (front) should be placed as close to the connector as possible. If possible, avoid placing label outside of the FDP. C6.3.9 Labels for Cat-X, DS-X cables should be placed within 4 inches of the connector. C6.3.10 Labels designating racks, cabinets, etc shall be P-Touch 3/4", white backing with bold black letters all capital.

C6.5.7 Fiber Distribution Panel (FDP) Labeling C6.5.7.1 All FDP's shall be labeled to identify their position within the relay rack/cabinet, the equipment connected to its ports and the CCSD/Circuit ID if applicable. C6.5.7.2 Most of the FDP's that DISA uses are position panels. Examples Fused Cables Only Signal Cables Only Fiber Optic Cables Only C6.4 Marked Drawing Requirements (REDLINES) C6.14.1 This section covers the requirements for correcting and updating installation documents and drawings. C6.14.2 The Installation Team shall ensure all work is completed in accordance with the detailed specifications or obtain approval from DISA NS6 if changes to the detailed specifications are required. C6.14.3 All installations, removals or assignment changes shall be marked on office base drawings, if applicable, and by electronic application (i.e., AutoCAD, VISIO, etc.). C6.14.4 The Installation Team shall compare the documents with the equipment layout and scope of work and make corrections as

DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 105

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
necessary so the "final" document package reflects the actual installation. C6.14.5 When a document or drawing is marked or corrected, there are associated documents that also require changes. the Installation Team shall correct all affected documents. C6.14.6 When corrections are required to the installation documents, the changes shall be legible and marked in color. Changes shall be made as detailed below: ˇ ˇ ˇ Red ­ Additions or changes shall be marked or highlighted in red. Yellow - Removals shall be marked or highlighted in yellow. Green or Blue - New information concerning existing equipment shall be marked or highlighted in green. This indicates a "Record Only" change.

C6.14.7 The Installation Team shall leave one copy of the redlined document package on-site and/or provide an electronic copy to the site POC. This copy is for "informational use only" and will not take the place of the "Final" document provided to the Customer. C6.14.8 When changes to the installation documents are required, the affected area shall be outlined in the appropriate color. It is not necessary to color the entire area. For example, an area outlined in red indicates that everything in that area has been added. However, everything possible shall be done to clarify the correction. Small areas (e.g., units mounted in a relay rack, added fuse, etc.) may be completely shaded; bay or circuit numbers may be colored over. C6.14.9 When a small area is outlined, it requires straight lines that define the affected area of equipment; a loose circle that covers part of the adjacent equipment shall not be used. However, large isolated areas may be circled, for example, if a complete bay or frame is being removed from a front equipment drawing, a circle may be used. The whole idea is to mark the drawing so the draftsperson can accurately update the drawings. C6.15 Parameters for Drawing Changes ­ Additions

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C6.15.1 Where there is enough space to legibly enter the information, the Installation Team shall: ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ Outline the exact area in red. Enter the information. Include locating dimensions. Use symbols to indicate bay sizes.

Circle the outlined area and draw a line to the intended location on the drawing. Enter the new information in the outlined area. Position the information exactly.

C6.15.3 Additions (red) and information (green) shall not be drawn on top of removals or changes (yellow). C6.17 Parameters for Drawing Changes ­ Changes C6.17.1 When equipment is to be replaced, the removal location shall be outlined or highlighted in yellow. C6.17.2 The Installation Team shall add the changes (new information and additions) using the rules detailed above for additions. Do not add the new equipment (red) over the removed (yellow) area. C7. C7.1 CHAPTER 7. AC and DC POWER

General Requirements

C7.1.1 Fiber paper, U-shaped fiber insulators, plastic grommet, sheathing, or other suitable materials shall be used to protect wire and cable that is being distributed off cable racks. The insulator or paper is to be secured in place with cable ties or other methods that ensure it remains in place. C7.1.2 Power wires shall be protected with fiber paper or acceptable plastic insulators where they pass through or come in contact with metal edged openings. C7.1.3 Fiber paper, U-shaped fiber insulators or plastic grommets are required around all metallic or other sharp edges of all cable paths. C7.1.4 Power cables shall be marked with their voltage and polarity near their termination points. Examples are: "-48 VDC" or "+48 VDC". C7.1.5 It is recommended when feasible, that the color of power cables used for distributing NEGATIVE DC voltage are BLACK and WHITE or RED and WHITE for the distribution of POSITIVE DC voltages. Large gauge cables 1/0 AWG or greater shall be marked with their respective voltage and polarity symbols at their ends. C7.1.6 Power racks and bays shall be installed plumb and level with the same allowable deviations listed in Table C7.1.1 of this standard. Frame Height 4' (137 7' (213 6" to 7' 0" cm to 213 cm) 0" to 9' 0" cm to 274 cm) 9' 0" (>274 cm) Maximum Allowable Deviation From Vertical Plumb 1/8" (3 mm) 3/16" (5 mm) 1/4" (6 mm)

Vertical Alignment of Power Racks and Bays Table 7.1.1

DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 110

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C7.1.7 DC power cables shall be run and secured on cable racks, power brackets, ducts, raceways, or conduits dedicated for their distribution. C7.1.8 AC and DC power cabling are not to be run on the same cable ladder or in the same duct. Maintain separation distances between AC power cables and twisted pair copper cables as specified in Table C7.1.2. Refer to NFPA 70, article 800 or applicable electrical codes for additional information. No separation distance is required when the data cables or the power cables are enclosed in a metallic raceway or conduit. C7.1.9 Power cables leaving cable racks and entering frames, racks, and other equipment shall have a maximum unsupported distance of 2 feet for cables 1/0 (53.4 mm2) and smaller. C7.1.10 Power cables leaving cable racks and entering frames, racks, and other equipment shall have a maximum unsupported distance of 3 feet for cables 1/0 (53.4 mm2) and larger. C7.1.11 Power cables are not to be laid or run across the surface of a floor. C7.1.12 Power cabling and wiring are not to be run directly from one cabinet or rack to another, except for rectifier/power board DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
wiring. A minimum of two dedicated 120 V nominal, non-switch AC duplex electrical outlet receptacles, each on a separate branch circuit, shall be provided for equipment power. The receptacles should be rated at 20 Amps and should be connected to a 20-amp branch circuit, unless otherwise directed in the installation plans. C7.1.13 AC power service in equipment racks shall be designated with name, number, voltage and type of service, therefore as an example: PWR DISTG SERVICE CAB 001 208V AC 60 HZ 3PH 4W C7.1.14 All AC outlets and light switches shall be designated with the location of the power source and circuit breaker number or inverter frame location. C7.2 DC Power Connectors and Connections

C7.2.1 Compression connectors shall be used on all power connections when possible. Mechanical connectors are permitted. Soldered connections are a last resort. C7.2.2 All connectors shall be sized and rated for the size and type of wire they are applied to. C7.2.3 Compression connectors 1/0 AWG (53.4 mm2) and larger are have two (2) hole type lugs whenever possible. Single hole lugs may be used by exception only when connecting to a stud in a power bay, or when the equipment specification requires a single hole lug. Recommend using a pneumatic crimping tool when installing compression connectors on a wire 1/0 AWG (53.4 mm2) or larger. C7.2.4 Lugs require lock and flat washers made of electrically compatible materials. Holes must be the proper size for the bolt or stud securing the lug. C7.2.5 When multiple crimps are required, the first crimp is to be towards the tang area of the connector and is to crimp the wire end. C7.2.6 The proper wire, connector, crimping tool, and die shall be used as a system to complete an acceptable crimp. The lug must be properly crimped.

DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 112

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C7.2.7 If the die generates comers or flashing, they must be thin and uniform. Excess flashing shall be removed and circular crimps shall be symmetrical. C7.2.8 Wires shall be fully inserted into the barrel of the connector. C7.2.9 A maximum length of 1/16"(2 mm) of exposed conductor between the cable insulation butt and the end of the lug is permissible. C7.2.10 Two-hole connectors are to have both holes used for fastening. C7.2.11 Lugs, punch-downs, or connectors designed to accommodate one lead are to have only one lead attached. C7.2.12 The Installation Team must verify that all manufacturer installed power connections are tight in accordance with the torque rating listed. C7.3 Bus Bars C7.3.1 Rack/cabinet bus bars shall be copper and be of a minimum dimension of 12 inches by 1 inch by 1/8 inch (3 mm), unless otherwise specified in the installation plan. C7.3.2 Any sharp edges or burrs shall be filed to insure good electrical contact and prevent personal injury. C7.3.3 Separations between bus bars of different potentials are not to be less than 3 inches (76 mm). C7.3.4 The separation between bus bars used for low frequency signal ground (up to 300 KHz) and cable rack, auxiliary framing, etc. are not to be less than one inch. C7.3.5 Insulators with metal inserts are to support the low frequency signal ground bus bars away from the rack or framing and provide a minimum of one mega-ohm resistance between the two conductors. Insulators shall be installed in accordance with the manufacturer's instructions, or as specified in the installation plan. C7.3.6 Equipment chassis or signal grounds shall be grounded to the respective bus bar with copper wire of 16 AWG or larger and DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 113

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
less than 3-feet in length or in accordance with the lengths listed in Table C7.3.1 or as directed by the installation plan. Cable Size(AWG) 8 10 12 14 16 Maximum Path Length 8ft (2.4 M) 5ft (1.5M) 3ft-2in (1.0M) 1ft-6in (0.5M) 10in (0.25M)

Maximum Length of Equipment Chassis Ground Cable Table C7.3.1 C7.3.7 Metal surfaces of equipment, frame and ground systems to be bonded in direct contact are to fall as close together in the galvanic series as possible. Compatible groupings of the common metals are given in Appendix B. The corrosive action between metals of different groups shall be greatest when the metallic union is openly exposed to salt spray, rain, or other liquids. The less exposed the bond, the less the rate of corrosion. C7.3.8 All connectors and bus bars shall be lightly cleaned with a mild abrasive prior to making connections. C7.3.9 All connections to bus bars shall be treated with a thin coat of anti-corrosion compound (e.g. NO-OX-ID-AŽ). C7.3.10 All connections to bus bars shall be made with 2 hole compression connectors or solder connectors of the proper size and type for the wire and threaded fastener. C7.3.11 All bolts, nuts, and washers used to fasten connectors to bus bars shall be silicon bronze or of electrochemically compatible metal such as brass or another copper alloy. Connections shall be adequately torqued. C7.3.12 Ground cables between the equipment and ground bus shall be terminated as indicated in following subparagraphs: C7.3.13 Termination of ground wire using a copper alloy (i.e. copper, brass, bronze) terminal lug onto an aluminum or steel chassis: Stainless steel flat washer or tooth lock-washer is placed between the terminal lug of the cable and equipment chassis. A stainless steel or copper alloy flat washer is placed on the opposite side of the connector followed by a stainless steel or copper alloy split-type lock washer. The DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 114

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
hardware is held in place by a stainless or copper alloy steel threaded fastener. Cover the connection with an anti-corrosive sealant if it is exposed to the weather or moisture. C7.3.14 Termination of ground wires on a copper bus: The connector shall be mounted directly onto the copper bus bar. A copper alloy or flat washer is then placed on the opposite side of the connector followed by a copper alloy lock washer. The hardware is held in place by a copper alloy threaded fastener. Finally, cover the connection with an anti-corrosive sealant if it is exposed to the weather or moisture. C7.3.15 Bond resistance between the ground wire connector and equipment chassis or ground bus is to be less than one milliohm. Resistance between equipment chassis or signal ground and the respective ground bus is to be less than five milli-ohms.

C7.4

Batteries and UPS

C7.4.1 Batteries shall be installed per the manufacturer's recommendations. Batteries are not required for a DISN Core facility if an existing UPS is used to feed the DC power plant, provided the UPS system has a four-hour battery backup capability. With fully redundant generators, the required UPS or DC power plant battery backup time is 5 minutes. C7.4.2 Battery banks with a capacity larger than 50 KVA shall be installed on open racks in battery rooms or areas that meet the criteria of MIL-HDBK-411B, TM5-684, Chapter 14, TM5-693, Section 4.1, IEEE-484, IEEE-485 and/or IEEE-1187. C7.4.3 It is permissible to install a battery bank with a capacity less than 50 KVA in cabinets and in the same room as the battery charger and inverter. C7.4.4 As a minimum, the room or area containing a battery bank is required to meet the safety and ventilation requirements of NFPA-70. Therefore, all rooms containing battery banks must provide sufficient ventilation to prevent the accumulation of hydrogen gas in the room's air. The ventilation equipment is to have the capacity to circulate the entire volume of the battery room or area air with fresh air from outside of the room at a rate of 2.5 times each hour. The objective of the room or ventilation is to keep the hydrogen concentration in the room air to less than 1 percent by volume. DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 115

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C7.4.5 The battery room's ambient temperature shall be maintained between 72°F and 82°F. The room shall have overtemperature and under-temperature alarms that are monitored remotely by duty personnel. C7.4.6 The designated battery room having batteries with liquid electrolyte shall have a floor drain with acid or alkaline proof piping leading to a collection tank located near the rack to permit the draining of spilled electrolyte, or a liquid tight fabricated basin underneath the battery bank. C7.4.7 The battery room's ambient temperature shall be maintained between 72°F and 82°F, the room shall have overtemperature and under-temperature alarms that are monitored remotely by duty personnel. C7.4.8 Battery cells shall be mounted only on a rack or group of racks specially constructed for this purpose. The racks shall be constructed of steel rails, frames, and braces. The battery cells are to rest on plastic channels and the rack is to be factory painted with an acid resistant paint. C7.4.9 The battery racks must be positioned and located in such a way as to allow access to the cells for periodic maintenance. C7.4.10 Per NEC insulation restrictions, battery strings are not to exceed 250 volts on any one rack. Ensure that sectionalizing protection is provided for each battery string. C7.4.11 Batteries having rubber jars shall be sectionalized into groups rated at 150 volts or less. C7.4.12 Battery racks, stands and cabinets shall be plumb and level. C7.4.13 Cells shall not be exposed to heating units, strip heaters, radiators, steam pipes, or sunlight. C7.4.14 Before installing cells onto a battery rack or into a battery cabinet, inspect cells for completeness of assembly, verification of nameplate, sizes and connection in accordance with applicable drawings. In addition, inspect for loose parts, leaks, damage, low electrolyte levels, intact vents sealed and plugs in place.

DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 116

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C7.4.15 The battery bank charger and inverters shall be assembled, positioned and located in accordance with the applicable drawings. C7.4.16 All straps are to align with the terminals without force. Batteries shall be moved or shimmed as necessary for alignment and to maintain level and plumb. C7.4.17 All straps and connections shall be tightened to the manufacturer's recommended torque and treated with a thin coat of anti-corrosion compound. C7.4.18 All connections and straps shall be clean and free of corrosion. C7.4.19 All cells shall be free of cracks and other damage. C7.4.20 The positive and negative battery leads must be run in separate non-metallic conduits. The cables from the normal and the alternate AC sources shall also be run in separate conduits. C7.4.21 The battery charger installation, supports, grounding and wiring must be in accordance with the applicable drawings. C7.4.22 The battery charger rating nameplate shall directly correspond with all applicable parameters of the AC supply to the charger and the electrical ratings of the battery to which it is connected. Check the settings of the charger and calibrate per the manufacturer's manual to match the battery recommended float and equalizing voltage levels. If the battery charger has been factory set, check the charger float and equalizing voltage levels against drawings and specifications. If the battery charger has not been factory set, set the charger float and equalizing voltage levels to those listed on drawings and specifications. The design criteria for DISN Core DC power systems is a discharge rate to 1.84 Volts per cell at the 4-hour rate. 44.16 volts is the minimum voltage supplied to DISN Core equipment for satisfactory operation. The float voltage should equal approximately 2.15 times the number of cells in the system. C7.4.23 Before connecting to the battery, measure and record the output voltage provided by the charger. C7.4.24 Verify and record that all charger functions and alarms operate correctly. DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 117

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C7.4.25 Measure the resistance and the quality of the cable insulation of all interconnecting cables between chargers, batteries and inverters in accordance with the following procedure: C7.4.26 Place the cable under test on a metal plate in a flat coil arrangement. Insulate the far-end of the cable with a plastic covering. Using a 6 AWG cable or a larger gauge, ground the plate to a known good grounding point. Connect one test lead of the mega-ohmmeter to the conductor of the cable. Connect the other test lead to the metallic plate. Ensure that a clock with a second hand is viewable from the test setup. Perform this test at temperatures ranging between 15°C and 25°C or approximately from 50°F to 80°F. Set the test voltage of the mega-ohmmeter to either 500 or 1000 VDC. C7.4.27 Vender shall ensure the proper High Voltage cable is utilized and meets the insulation resistance required for safe utilization in accordance with manufacturer specifications. C7.4.28 After assembly, torque terminal connections shall be in accordance with manufacturer specifications. Coat terminals with a protective coating of an anticorrosion compound. The compound is to completely seal the bond between the strap and the terminal, and the attaching hardware. There is to be no excessive compound on the straps, or globs of excess compound. C7.4.29 Verify when the battery is fully charged and record the time to charge. C7.4.30 After the battery is completely charged, measure and record the total voltage across the battery and between each adjacent cell. The total voltage should approximately be the resultant of the quantity of cells multiplied by the typical cell voltage. A variation is an indication that the battery bank may be improperly assembled. C7.4.31 Measure and record each cell's internal ohmic values and the inter-cell connection resistances. This is accomplished by either a battery impedance tester or by applying a load across the battery and measuring the step change in voltage and current for each cell taken between the positive and negative terminal posts of adjacent cells as well as the battery as a whole. The ohmic value is the change in voltage divided by the change in current. The resistance values for each cell should be averaged and any interconnection that varies no more than 10 percent from DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 118

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
the accumulated average resistance of all measured cells. Inspect wet and VRLA cells for cleanliness, corrosion, sulfurication and leakage. Pay particular attention to measuring those cells with visable corrosion or leakage. Record cell conductivities and voltages deviating more than 10 percent from the average value of the string cells measured. C7.4.32 Measure and record the following parameters of each cell: voltage in the float mode, specific gravity, negative terminal temperature and visually checked electrolyte level. C7.4.33 Measure and record total battery voltage with charger in float mode of operation, ac ripple current, overall float voltage at the battery terminals, charger output current and voltage, and the ambient temperature. C7.4.34 All cells shall be numbered and appropriate covers shall be in placed upon completion of installation. C7.4.35 Float voltage is to be maintained unless otherwise specified in writing by a DISA CONUS Engineer. C7.4.36 Initial battery cell readings shall be taken using battery report forms during installation. C7.4.37 A copy of the report is to be provided to DISA NS6. aditional copy is to be left in a protective binder and maintained with the battery bank throughout its life cycle. C7.5 Fuses and Circuit Breakers An

C7.5.1 All fuses and circuit breakers shall comply with the general requirements for overcurrent protection and overcurrent protective devices not more than 600 volts, specified in Article 240, Parts I through VII, of the National Electric Code. C7.5.2 Cartridge type fuses are to have the ferrules and blades of the holder coated with a thin coat of conductive anticorrosion compound. C7.5.3 Link type fuses are to have the contact area of the fuse and the blades of the holder coated with a thin coat of conductive anti-corrosion compound. C8. C8.1

CHAPTER 8.

Grounding requirements

General Requirements

C8.1.1 A DISN facility ground system is to be composed of the following four subsystems with the exception of facilities located in the Arctic and Antarctic regions: ˇ ˇ ˇ ˇ Earth Electrode Lightning Protection Fault Protection Signal Reference

C8.1.2 All subsystems are to meet the criteria of MIL-STD-188124 and the guidelines MIL-HDBK-419A. Where conflicts in the standards exist, the more stringent requirement shall be used. DISA equipment and systems are not to be installed at facilities that do not meet the above requirement without the approval of DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 120

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
DISA NS6. Facilities that receive a waiver are to submit a plan for correcting all cited discrepancies within 30 days after receiving the waiver to DISA NS6. C8.1.3 The Site Concurrence Letter should request the Site provide and install the AC Power connections required for the installation of the DISN equipment. C8.1.4 The Site Concurrence Letter should request the Site provide a dedicated ground for the DISN. This will enable the ground reference to be as close to True ground as possible. C8.2 Earth Electrode Subsystem.

C8.2.1 Engineering drawings accurately illustrate the physical dimension and layout of the EES. The EES engineering drawing is to show the location of the following items: ground rods, grids, plates, interconnecting conductors, ground wells, ground reference point and EES connecting points. C8.2.2 All modifications to the EES shall be shown in a dated and approved revision for the system installation drawing, or RED-LINE into the current installation drawing. C8.2.3 Review the earth resistance measurements of the earth electrode system in accordance with the fall-of-potential method as described in Volume II, Section 2.7.2 and Volume 2, Section 2.2.2.2.1 of MIL-HDBK-419A. The earth resistance measurement of the EES must have been performed at least three months after the EES was back filled. Figures C8.2.2 and C8.2.23 show samples of a drawing and worksheet from a sample test report of a properly performed resistance to earth measurement of an EES. C8.2.4 The fall-of-potential earth resistance measurement of the EES is to be less than 5 ohms. C8.3 Lightning Protection System

C8.3.1 Air terminals must extend at least 25 cm (10 inches) directly above the object that it is protecting. C8.3.2 Coaxial lines and waveguides between the antenna and the associated transmit/receive equipment shall be grounded as stated in the subparagraphs following.

DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 121

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
C8.3.3 Each transmission line shall be bonded to the down conductor of the tower's air terminal at the top near its antenna and at the bottom near the vertical to horizontal transition point from the tower. C8.3.4 Transmission lines are also to be bonded to the antenna tower at the same points, as well as at intervals of approximately every 30 meters when the tower exceeds 60 meters (200 feet). C8.3.5 All transmission lines, conduit or piping entering a building must be bonded to the entry plate as shown in Figure C8.3.1. C8.3.6 Lightning surge arrestors shall be installed on all power lines entering a building, normally at the facility main disconnect point found typically in the main electrical distribution panel. C8.3.7 All metallic signal/data lines entering the building that shall be terminated to surge arrestors at the main distribution frame shall be near the cable entrance panel.

C8.4 Fault Protection Subsystem

C8.4.1 Fault protection ground wires are not to be used to conduct normal load currents and are only to be used to conduct line to ground fault currents. C8.4.2 All single-phase electric power receptacles shall have three wires, including a safety ground, neutral and phase. C8.4.3 Refer to the illustration of a NEMA-15 electrical outlet in Figure C8.4.1. Note that the Phase slot is smaller in size than the Neutral slot. Dependent on the normal voltage setting of the regional electrical provider or the setting of the inverters of the facility's UPS, the Phase-to-Neutral voltage shall range from 108 to 125 VAC. The voltage between the Ground-to-Neutral conductors is not to exceed 2 VAC. The voltage between the Neutral-to-Phase is to be approximately the sum or difference of the Neutral-to-Phase and Ground-to-Neutral voltage.

C8.4.4 Using a clamp-on current probe with all equipment installed and operational, measure and record the current on the main fault-protection ground line in the circuit breaker box that is providing power to the newly installed equipment. If the current on the ground line exceeds one-amp, notify the responsible party on-site and DISA NS6. C8.5 Signal Ground Reference

C8.5.1 Low frequency signal ground reference systems, such as a single-point ground bus (overhead copper bus-bars or large gauge uninsulated bus cable routed under a raised floor) shall not be installed in new DISN Facilities due to their poor performance in conducting high frequency noise emissions to ground. In the event that a low-frequency ground reference system was previously installed, contact DISA NS6 for further instructions. C8.5.2 Only high frequency signal ground reference systems shall be installed in new DISN Facilities, unless otherwised authorized by DISA NS6. A high frequency signal reference typically consists of the three primary components: equipotential plane, equipment ground conductors, and structural steel elements and electrical supporting structures, connected to the earth electrode subsystem. C8.5.3 Document what types of equipotential planes are utilized in the facility. C8.5.4 The structural steel of the building is to be connected to the earth electrode subsystem with 1/0 AWG copper cables. C8.5.5 The distance between adjacent connections from the building structure to the earth electrode subsystem should not exceed 15 meters (50 feet). C8.5.6 In buildings where steel frame construction is not used, a supplemental network must be installed consisting of large copper cables conforming to Table C8.5.1 below. C8.5.7 Equipment racks, electrical supporting structures, and utility pipes shall be connected to this structural steel of the building or copper cable grid of the equipotential plane with #6 AWG copper wire. C8.5.8 This interconnecting wire should be as short as feasible, and not exceeding 24 inches to minimize high frequency reactance. DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

C8.5.11 If an overhead equipotential plane is utilized, because it is impractical to install a plane on the floor around the equipment ensure: ˇ ˇ ˇ The overhead equipotential plane is fabricated from screening or sheets of metal. The overhead equipotential plane is fabricated from a grid with a 4-inch or less spacing. The grounding cables from the equipment racks to the overhead plane shall be 3 feet or less in length.

C8.5.12 The plane shall be bonded to the main structural steel members of the building at multiple locations. The structural steel shall in turn be bonded to the earth electrode subsystem. C8.6 Routing, Supporting, and Securing Grounding Conductors

C8.6.1 Signal or equipotential planes grounding conductors are not to be run on top of cable racks, or next to power, signal or control lines. Ground conductors shall be run in such a manner as to facilitate visual inspection of the conductors. C8.6.2 Signal or equipotential plane grounding conductors shall be routed in straight paths unless not feasible due to rack, equipment or partition layout. C8.6.3 Changes in signal or equipotential plane grounding conductor direction are not to exceed 90 degrees and have a radius greater than 8 inches (20 cm). C8.6.4 Racks/cabinets shall be grounded to the EES by a six AWG (13.3 mm2) wire or larger, in accordance with Table C8.6.1 of this document. The ground wires from rack/cabinet to the EES are not to exceed three feet in length. They shall be terminated to rack/cabinet ground buses and to conductors of the EES that are size 1/0 AWG (53.5 mm2) or greater. A recommended grounding option is to attach a copper ground bar or copper strip to the rack for grounding equipment. Two-hole lugs should be used for secure grounding of equipment. Removing paint at the point of contact in the equipment with Type "B" tooth lock DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

washers is an acceptable commercial practice, as long as a bonding resistance of 1 milliohm is not exceeded. Bonding on all four sides of the rack is required and each cabinet should be connected to the signal grounding infrastructure with an AWG6 copper conductor that is less than six feet in length. C8.6.9 Ground leads are not to be completely enclosed by metal, i.e. conduit, threaded rod, etc. When this is unavoidable, both ends of the conduit etc. shall be bonded to the ground lead. C8.7 Termination of Ground Conductors

C8.7.1 An anti-corrosion compound (e.g. NO-OX-ID-AŽ) is required on all external ground connections. C8.7.2 All ground connections shall be clean, secure, and have a bond resistance less than 1 milli-ohm. C8.7.3 Non-conductive coatings such as paint shall be stripped from an area one and a half times the size of the contact area of the lug to expose bare metal before a ground lead is terminated to a particular piece of equipment, frame or structure. C8.7.4 Two-hole compression connectors of the proper size for the wire and bus bar are required on all ground bus bars unless otherwise specified by the installation plans. C8.7.5 All ground conductors shall be copper and terminated with two-hole compression connectors unless otherwise specified by the installation plans. One-hole connectors may be used to ground equipment shelves, etc. C8.7.6 All armored inner duct and metal stiffening members shall be grounded where they first enter the building or cable vault. C8.7.7 Ensure that all cabinets, cable ladder and metal ducting are grounded to the earth electrode subsystem. C8.7.8 All structures such as conduits, cable trays, ducts, power enclosures, and other conductive members longer than 4 feet shall be grounded to the EES at multiple points. They must be grounded regardless of whether they contain a power or signal cable. All fittings must be tight and covers securely fastened. All grounding lock nuts or toothed lock washers must penetrate paint or other non-conductive finishes. Structures shall be connected to the equipotential plane or signal reference subsystem within 24 inches (61 cm) of each end of a run and at intervals, not to exceed 50 feet (15 M). C8.7.9 Proper wire sizes, identified in the installation plans, shall be used. The wire must not be smaller than the indicated minimum size and must provide at least 500 cmil (0.25 mm 2) cross DISN IMPLEMENTATION STANDARDS

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

Page 129

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
sectional area per running foot (30 cm) for trunk ground cable and at least 2000 cmil (1 mm2) cross sectional area per running foot (30 cm) for all other signal ground cables. C8.8 Grounding Conductor Identification

Ground leads shall be identified at all common ground points, such as at the Station Ground Bar (SGB) or Telecommunications Master Ground Busbar (TMGB). Grounding installation shall be in accordance with the NEC NFPA 70 National Electrical Code, 2005. Proper grounding is a life safety requirement and shall not be waived. The contractor shall install a Telecommunications Master Ground Busbar (TMGB) at the DISN site cable entrance area(s). The TMGB shall be connected to the building's main power ground busbar with the appropriate sized cable having a green jacket with a yellow stripe, installed in an appropriate conduit, if required, to protect the cabling. C8.8.1 A "Do Not Disconnect" tag is to be attached to each end of all grounding conductors extending between the signal ground subsystem and the earth electrode subsystem. C9. CHAPTER 9. COAX GROUNDING C9.1 WAVEGUIDE, RIDGED-COAX, AND SEMI-RIDGED

General Requirements

C9.1.1 All waveguides, ridged coax and semi-ridged coax (Helix) shall be grounded in four locations as follows: (1) To the nearest grounding point behind the respective antenna. (2) At the base of the antenna tower as the transmission line bends 90 degrees from a vertical to a horizontal transition. (3) At the entrance to the building near the transmission line feed-through panel. (4) At every 100 foot (33 M) or shorter intervals along the length of the tower. C9.1.2 Grounding kits specified by the manufacturer of the waveguides, ridged coax or semi-ridged coax shall be used. Transmission line grounding kits shall be installed in accordance with the manufacturer's instruction, as specified by the engineering drawings and installation plans. C9.1.3 The metallic supporting structures for the waveguides shall be electrically continuous and connected to the exterior Earth Electrode System (EES) with a minimum of 6 AWG (13.3 mm2) wire at the first and last support columns. (The wire leads shall be as direct as possible). C9.1.4 All transmission lines shall be properly bonded to the entrance panel. The entrance panel is to be connected by the most direct route to the EES using a 1/0­AWG (53.5 mm2) or larger stranded copper cable. The bonding resistance between the entrance panel and the EES is to be less than five milli-ohms. C9.1.5 The air-dielectric of the waveguide and coaxial line is to be pressurized between 3 and 8 PSI (20 ­ 55 KPa) with dry air or nitrogen. C9.1.6 The dry-air system for the air-dielectric is to provide an audible alarm to a manned monitoring position for the following conditions: the relative humidity of the airdielectric has exceeded 8%, the air pressure of the air dielectric is less than 2 PSI (14 KPa), the air pressure of the air dielectric is more than 9 PSI (62 KPa).

C10. CHAPTER 10. Documentation

C10.1 General Requirements C10.1.1 Upon completion of the installation, the Vendor's installation team shall provide up-to-date marked engineering drawings, also referred to as "REDLINE DRAWINGS," to their engineering support team. The Redline Drawings shall show all changes or deviations from the original approved engineering drawings. Changes or deviations shall be recorded on all corresponding drawings, i.e.: block diagrams, cable/wire/run lists, floor plans, interconnecting diagrams, network architect drawings, rack-face elevations and system diagrams. The following color scheme is to be used for indicating changes: C10.1.2 RED: Equipment addition or changes, assignment changes, cable rerouting or changes. C10.1.3 YELLOW HIGHLIGHT: Equipment or cabling removal or relocation. C10.1.4 BLUE: Text information on changes representing new information that affects existing records, but does not reflect equipment being removed or added. C10.1.5 As part of the completion report submission, the Vendor's engineering support team shall reflect the Redline Drawing information in the final "AS-BUILT" drawing submitted to NS6 and the DISA Configuration Management Team as an update to DISA's Network Configuration and Change Management tool (NCCM). C10.1.6 Installation teams shall ensure proper hand over to DISA Operations for monitoring and maintaining the installed system and not depart the site until released by DISA Operations after their acceptance of system.

Electrical Power Quality Instructions The following electrical power quality characteristics shall be measured and recorded: RMS Voltage (VRMS), Peak Voltage Vpk, RMS Amperage (ARMS), Peak Amperage (APk), Line Frequency, Voltage Total Harmonic Distortion (VTHD) , Current Total Harmonic Distortion (ITHD), Real Power (KW), Apparent Power (KVA), Reactance Power (KVAR) Power Factor (PF), voltage swell, voltage transients, voltage sags, To measure and record frequently occurring abnormalities of the selected location's electrical power quality it is strongly recommended that the duration of a power quality test is at least week long. The minimum duration of an electrical power quality test shall be eight ­ hours. The power quality test shall be conducted at the power panels in which the planned system(s) derive its power from. In addition the site's emergency generator system shall be brought on line using its automatic start function and shall power the selected site. The power analyzer's measuring location shall be relocated to the power input of the UPS The generator system shall power the site for at least an hour, but no longer then four hours. The selected power quality analyzer (and measurement recorder) shall have at least an one hour battery backup and the capability of measuring and recording the electrical parameters list in Instruction 1 at their possible minimum and maximum magnitude. In the test data sheets provide the initial, maximum and minimum measurement of each parameter.

14. 15. 16.

Pass-Fail and Report Specifications: VRMS differences between phases shall not exceed ą2% of the mean; Neutral to ground VRMS voltage shall not exceed 2% of the phase VRMS; Report ARMS differences between phases when they exceed ą10% of mean; ARMS differences between phases shall not exceed ą10% of mean at the output of a transformer; ARMS on the ground shall not exceed 0.1 ARMS VTHD% shall not exceed 5% on phases. Report ITHD% that exceed 20% on a phase. ITHD% shall not exceed 35% on phases. Power factor shell be greater than 85%. Line frequency is within a half of cycle of the standard line frequency of the the region of 50 Hz or 60 Hz. Steady state voltage shall not exceed ą10% normal VRMS. Line shall be less than 120% of normal and shall not exceed 0.5 seconds in duration. Transients shall be less 200% of normal VPk, shall have a ringing frequency less than 5 KHz, and shall have duration of less than 3 milliseconds. Voltage sags greater than 80% of normal VRMS shall have, shall have a duration of less then 10 seconds; Voltage sags greater than 70% but less than 80% of normal VRMS shall have, shall have a duration of less then 0.5 seconds; Voltage dropouts shall be less then 20 milliseconds long in duration.

Test results provided by site's power support team or previous implementations power survey may be utilized if less than two years old. If test results are older or unavailable, request the site have their power tested before completing site survey. If the site is unable to conduct a power survey before the site survey begings, the implementations vendor may perform a power survey to utilize. The results from the power and grounding tests shall be compared to the equipment manufacturer's specifications to determine site suitability. If the site is unsuitable for DISN suite installation, notify DISA NS-6 immediately for escalation and go/nogo decision.

Appendix C. DISN INSTALLATION QUICK REFERENCE CHECKLIST
Description 1. Verify that there is adequate HVAC. Reference: ASHRAE 90429 2. Inspect area under the raised floor or over a suspended ceiling to ensure there are no power runs or HVAC venting, making the space unusable. Reference: Chapter 1 3. Check that there is a minimum of 36" of space in front, rear and 24" on side if it is the end of a rack. Reference: Chapter 2 4. Ensure cable exits a conduit only through a connector or bushing, and not through the unprotected end of a conduit. Reference: Chapter 1 5. Lighting at wire closets or distribution frames shall be at least 50-foot candle. Reference: Chapter 1 6. Fiber carrying secure (RED) communication is to be incased in metallic conduits or ducting and separated from BLACK communication. Reference: Chapter 4 7. Cable ducts, ladders and trays are to be installed plumb or level, except when changing elevations with 45-degree elbows. Reference: Chapter 1 8. The diameter of the ground cable at least 2000 cmil (1X10-6 M2) per running foot. The minimum gauge of a ground cable for frame is 6 AWG. Reference: Chapter 8 9. Resistance between equipment chassis or signal ground and respective ground bus is less than 5 milliohms. Reference: Chapter 8 10. The measured earth resistance of the earth electrode system of any DISN facility is less than 5 ohms, IAW the Fall-Of-Potential method. Reference: Chapter 8 11. Ensure all doors open and close properly. Reference: Chapter 1 12. Rack design and its electronic equipments are positioned for good thermal cooling, natural air convection, or forced air convection from internal fans. An infrared thermometer or thermal image camera does not detect hot-spots that would be detrimental to the operation rack's electronic equipment. Reference: Chapter 2 13. Separation of adjacent equipment within a rack is in accordance with engineering drawings and installation plan. Top and bottom interval spacing of at least 1.75 inches unless otherwise specified by the installation plan. Reference: Chapter 1 PASS FAIL N/A Comments

C1

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY
Description 14. Slotted Channel is anchored directly to the flooring at intervals no greater than 2˝ feet (76cm). Reference: Chapter 2 15. All Slotted Channel is cut squarely. All exposed ends are finished with an end cap. Reference: Chapter 2 16. Threads on bolts, cap screws, machine screws, rods and similar threaded parts are engaged through to the final thread of the Slotted Channel (spring) nut. Reference: Chapter 2 17. Threaded rods are fastened to the Slotted Channel using a flat washer, lock washer and nut. Reference: Chapter 2 18. All bolts, nuts, and screws are tight. Reference: Chapter 2 19. All conduits are installed in accordance with engineering specifications and drawings called out in the installation plan. Reference: Chapter 2 20. All unused knockouts of raceways, electrical boxes and cabinets are closed or covered. Reference: Chapter 1 21. Conduits are placed so as not to block future cabling and equipment installations. Reference: Chapter 2 22. All conduits are grounded at their far ends. In cases where a conduit run exceeds 133 feet (40 meters) the conduit is grounded at least every 100 feet (30 meters) with 2 AWG stranded copper wire. Reference: Chapter 2 23. All conduit supports are the proper size, type and material for the application. They are installed correctly in accordance with engineering drawings and as specified by the installation plan. All conduits are bent to conform to the supporting structure. Reference: Chapter 2 24. Ducts and raceways are supported at least every 5 feet (1.5 meters) and within 2 feet (61 cm) of each end. Reference: Chapter 2 25. All ducts and raceways are installed plumb or level, except when changing elevations with 45-degree elbows. Reference: Chapter 2 26. All duct and raceway fittings are assembled IAW manufacturer's instructions or as specified by the engineering drawings and installation plan. Reference: Chapter 2 27. The edges of wire access cutouts in ducts and raceways are covered with plastic grommet or other suitable protective material. Reference: Chapter 2 PASS FAIL N/A Comments

Description 28. Ducting, raceways, and ladder racking are electrically continuous by bonding together all sections and covers. Quality Assurance Surveillance Plan (QASP)
1. Contract Title: DISN Optical Network Enhancement Link 38 2. Work Requirements: The Performance Work Statement (PWS) defines requirements for the Contractor to provide dark fiber, equipment, and commercial facilities to support Department of Defense (DOD) users in the Continental United States (CONUS). The PWS further defines requirements for the Contractor to install, integrate, and test Optical Line Amplifier (OLA), Junction, and service delivery node (SDN), equipment and provide Operations and Maintenance (O&M) support in commercial fiber facilities. In addition, the PWS defines the requirements for the Contractor to provide end-to-end transmission and professional support services to include, but not limited to, Defense Information Systems Network (DISN) diversity and resiliency capabilities, system integration, and system upgrades. 3. Primary Method of Surveillance: The Government primary method of surveillance for all tasks within the PWS shall be:  100 Percent Inspection. This is usually only the most appropriate method for infrequent tasks or tasks with stringent performance requirements, e.g., where safety or health is a concern. With this method, performance is inspected/evaluated at each occurrence. One hundred percent inspection is too expensive to be used in most cases.  Periodic Inspection: These services are monitored weekly, monthly, quarterly, semiannually, annually, etc. Intermittent types of activities are perfect for periodic inspection because not only are they infrequent, but there is normally a predetermined, specified time frame within which the tasks must be accomplished. Therefore, you know exactly when to conduct the evaluations. Periodic inspections automatically become 100 percent evaluations or "100 percent checks." Inspections should be divided and scheduled by frequency: annual, semiannual, quarterly, monthly, weekly and as required. Sometimes services are required for which the time or frequency cannot be predicted, such as accident investigations, one-time special tasking by higher headquarters, etc. These would be labeled "as required inspections." Others are known and predictable, such as the quarterly status report or the monthly travel report currently included in some DISA service contracts.  Customer Input. Although usually not a primary method, this is a valuable supplement to more systematic methods. For example, in a case where random sampling indicates unsatisfactory service, customer complaints can be used as substantiating evidence. In certain situations where customers can be relied upon to complain consistently when the quality of performance is poor, e.g., dining facilities, building services, customer surveys and customer complaints may be a primary surveillance method, and customer satisfaction an appropriate performance standard. In all cases, complaints should be documented, preferably on a standard form. 4. Scope of Performance: The scope of this contract includes all services and supplies necessary to perform the objective, to include programmatic, engineering, and other technical services and the procurement of all necessary equipment and components.

UNCLASSIFIED//FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

UNCLASSIFIED//FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY QASP OTN Upgrade Page 2 of 3

5. Performance Standards: The Contractor shall adhere adhere to all prevailing telecommunications industry standards during the execution of the PWS. Performance Standard Deliverables are submitted on time and the Contractor manages performance of the overall requirement in accordance with the Project Schedule. Contractor ensures performance of all tasks meet the requirements of the PWS and standard DISA requirements (e.g TSRs, SCLs). Acceptable Quality Level (AQL) Deliverables contain required information and are delivered on time at least 90% of the time. Revisions that occur are minor and are resolved in a satisfactory manner. Schedules and provided implementation plans are accurate 90% of the time. Issues that occur are minor and are resolved in a satisfactory manner. All installation will be of the same quality as similar equipment in the same facility Random inspection of installations will be conducted. Method of Surveillance Random inspection of deliverable products and services.

OLA installations will conform to accepted Telecom practice for other installations in contractor facilities Testing and test data will meet manufactures requirements to ensure the equipment functions as designed System integration will be acceptable when the link passes the 72 hour Bit Error Rate (BER) test with no errors

All test data will be provided to the government engineering team and GNSC for review and historical records. All test data will be provided to the government engineering team and GNSC for review prior to any service being activated.

The Government will perform random review of the test data to ensure it complies with equipment manufactures requirements. 100% inspection of and acceptance of all test data prior to any service activation.

6. Mandatory or regulatory compliance items: The Contracting Officer Representative will monitor compliance as required by clause 52.222-50, Combating Trafficking in Persons, and report any issues to the Contracting Officer. 7. Acceptable Quality Level (AQL): The Contractor must deliver the enhancement as specified by the Government, and all equipment must function in accordance with its intended purpose to produce an overall effective communications system. The AQLs for this project are stated in paragraph 5.
UNCLASSIFIED//FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY

UNCLASSIFIED//FOR OFFICIAL USE ONLY QASP OTN Upgrade Page 3 of 3

8. Evaluation Method: The Government shall use the monitoring methods cited to determine whether the performance standards/service level/AQLs have been met. If the Contractor has not met the minimum requirements, the Contractor may be asked to develop a corrective action plan to show how and by what date the Contractor intends to bring performance up to the required levels. 9. Incentives (Positive and/or Negative): If performance standards are not met, the Contracting Officer may seek any remedy available under the terms and conditions of the contract. If response and/or repair times for fiber/equipment failure are longer than required by the PWS, the Contractor shall grant the Government a maintenance credit as specified in the Outage Clause of Section H.
