Section M - Evaluation Factors for Award

SECTION M
Evaluation Factors for Award


M001 SOURCE SELECTION

      a. Basis for Contract Award

Award will be made to the offeror whose proposal is determined to represent the overall best value to the government using a lowest-priced
technically acceptable evaluation process.  Source selection will be conducted in accordance with Federal Acquisition Regulation (FAR) 15 as
supplemented by the Defense Federal Acquisition Regulation Supplement (DFARS), and the DISA Acquisition Regulation Supplement (DARS).  These
regulations are available electronically at http://www.ditco.disa.mil/hq/aqinfo.asp and http://farsite.hill.af.mil.

The Government will make award based upon an acceptability assessment of compliance with solicitation requirements, technical/management, and
price.  To be eligible for award, the proposal must conform to the solicitation’s requirements (to include all stated terms, conditions,
representations, certifications, and all other information required by Section L of this solicitation).  The proposal must meet all technical
evaluation criteria set forth below in order to be determined technically acceptable.  The price proposed must be determined reasonable and the
Offeror must be deemed responsible in accordance with the FAR, as supplemented, in order to be eligible for award.  The Source Selection
Authority (SSA) will base the source selection decision on an integrated assessment of the proposal against all source selection criteria in the
solicitation (described below).

      b. Evaluation

The proposal should include all information the Offeror wants the Government to consider and evaluate regarding its company’s ability to perform
all required tasks and conform to all required terms and conditions.  The evaluation of the proposal will be based on the stated evaluation
factors.

After receipt of proposals, the Government will first evaluate the lowest price proposal.  If the lowest price proposal is determined to be
technically acceptable and otherwise properly awardable, no further evaluations will be conducted, and award will be made.  If, however, the
lowest price proposal is determined to be technically unacceptable and/or otherwise not properly awardable, further evaluations will be
conducted.

      c. Evaluation of Options

The Government will evaluate offers for award purposes by adding the total price for all options to the total price for the base period.  The
Offeror shall submit pricing for the base period and all option periods, including option pricing for an additional six-month period that may be
authorized in accordance with FAR 52.217-8.  See FAR 52.217-8 which authorizes the Government to require continued performance of any services
within the limits and at the rates specified in the contract.  The pricing proposal should include a separate line item for the additional six-
month period in accordance with FAR 52.217-8.  These prices shall be identical to the proposed pricing in the six months prior to expiration of
the base period or the final option period, if option periods are present.  The total evaluated price will consist of the Offeror’s proposed
price for the base period, all option periods, and the option pricing for the additional six-month period.  The Government may determine that an
offer is unacceptable if the option prices are significantly unbalanced.  Evaluation of options shall not obligate the Government to exercise
the option(s).

      d. Number of Contracts to be Awarded

The Government intends to award one (1) fixed-price contract; however, the Government reserves the right to make no award at all.

      e. Rejection of Offers

The Government may reject any proposal that is evaluated to be nonviable in terms of program commitments, contract terms and conditions.
Additionally, the Government may reject proposals that are exceptionally high or low in cost when compared to Government estimates, such that
the proposal is deemed to reflect an inherent lack of competence or failure to comprehend the complexity and risks of the program.

M002 EVALUATION FACTORS

     a. Evaluation Factors and Subfactors

            The following evaluation factors and subfactors will be used to evaluate each proposal.  An award will not be made to a proposal that
is not technically acceptable in all of the evaluation factors and subfactors described below.

      Factor 1: Technical/Management: In order to be found technically acceptable, the offeror must demonstrate its ability to perform in all of
      the following areas, including all Subfactors:


          Subfactor 1: Program Management (PWS Paragraph 6 (6.1-6.4))
          Subfactor 2: Implementation of a new 100G P-OTN segment (PWS Paragraph 6 (6.5-6.6))
          Subfactor 3: Operations and Maintenance (PWS Paragraph 6 (6.7-6.9))

      Factor 2: Price Factor




M003 EVALUATION CRITERIA

       a. Factor 1: Technical/Management Factor

           1) Subfactor 1: Program Management


In order for this subfactor to be rated Acceptable, the Offeror’s proposal must demonstrate their ability to provide the services and
deliverables required under PWS requirements, Paragraph 6 (6.1 – 6.4), Task Area 1:  Program management.  The contractor must be capable of
performing the program management activities defined in the PWS including program planning, design, coordination, control, reporting, and
meetings.

           2) Subfactor 2: Implementation of a new 100G P-OTN segment


In order for this subfactor to be rated Acceptable, the Offeror’s proposal must demonstrate their ability to provide the services and
deliverables required under PWS requirements, Paragraph 6 (6.5 and 6.6), Task Area 2: Implementation of a new 100G P-OTN segment.  The
contractor must be able to Engineer, Furnish, Install, Secure, Test (EFIST) and make operational a new 100G 6500 P-OTN consisting of fiber,
amplifier and SDN locations detailed in the CONUS Site Specific MBOM.  The proposal must demonstrate that the Offeror understands the scope and
complexity of meeting the Government requirements for repairing and replacing dark fiber detailed in the PWS and Functional Requirements
Specification (FRS), as well as the technical requirements detailed in the PWS and FRS.


The Offeror’s proposal must demonstrate their ability to acquire and provide acceptable tested and IRU fiber (2 strands) from:


    • Tinker Air Force Base (AFB), OK Building 3900 or 3001.  From Tinker AFB the route must connect to Fort Sill, OK Building 1645 or 462.


               • If Building 1645 is chosen as the starting point above, the route must continue from Fort Sill, OK, Building 462 and connect to
                 Barksdale AFB, LA (Building 3447 or 7212). If Building 462 is chosen as the starting point above, the route must continue from
                 Fort Sill, OK, Building 1645 and connect to Barksdale AFB, LA (Building 3447 or 7212).


    • From Barksdale AFB, LA the route must connect to Fort Polk, LA (bldg. 1830).


    • From Fort Polk, LA the route must terminate at Keesler AFB, MS (bldg. 1101).


           3) Subfactor 3: Operations and Maintenance


In order for this subfactor to be rated Acceptable, the Offeror’s proposal must demonstrate their ability to provide the services and
deliverables required under PWS requirements, Paragraph 6 (6.7 – 6.9), Task Area 3:  Operation and Maintenance and Sustainment services for
fiber and associated assets.  The offeror’s proposal must demonstrate their ability to provide and perform all the requirements necessary for
sustainment of all IRU assets and associated co-location facilities and equipment. This entails, but may not be limited to, backbone fiber,
associated co-location facilities, and end-to-end transmission for Service Delivery Nodes (SDNs) within commercial and Government facilities.

The proposal must demonstrate an Operations and Maintenance approach that provides the processes, procedures, and controls to ensure performance
and maintenance requirements of PWS will be met.  The proposal must address support for corrective and preventative maintenance 24 hours a day,
7 days a week, 365 days a year for fiber and associated facilities. Offeror must provide an equipment sparing plan that details how much spare
equipment will be required and managed for maintenance purposes based on, but not limited to, the equipment manufacturer’s failure rate Mean
Time Between Failures (MTBF), the response and restoral times, and the Contractor’s field experience.


      b. Price Factor

            (1) The offeror’s price proposal will be evaluated for award purposes based upon the total price proposed for basic requirements
(basic award) and all options, including option pricing for an additional 6-month period that may be authorized IAW FAR 52.217-8, as specified
in Schedule B and related pricing template (Attachment J7 Pricing Template) of the RFP.  The Cost/Price volume will consist of a Government-
provided Attachment J7 Pricing Template in Section J which shall be utilized by the Offerors for pricing their proposals.  With the exception of
selected cells within the "Link 38 Pricing Template" tab of Attachment J7 Pricing Template, the Pricing Template is protected by the Government
and offerors shall not unprotect, alter or add to the Pricing Template in any manner not directed in the instructions.

                 (2) Evaluation of options shall not obligate the Government to exercise such options.

            (3) The offeror’s price proposal will be evaluated, using one or more of the techniques defined in FAR 15.404, in order to determine
if it is reasonable and complete.  Normally, price reasonableness is established through price analysis techniques as described in FAR 15.404.
For additional information see FAR 31.201-3.  For a price to be complete, all solicitation requirements must be priced, figures correctly
calculated and costs presented in the Government-provided pricing template.  Offerors should not include additional technical data in Volume III
- Cost/Price to include Attachment J7 Pricing Template and any supplemental summaries. Technical data should only be included in Volume II of
the offeror's proposal.

M004 SOLICITATION REQUIREMENTS, TERMS AND CONDITIONS

Offerors are required to meet all solicitation requirements, such as terms and conditions, representations and certifications, and
technical/management requirements, in addition to those identified as factors or subfactors.  Failure to comply with the terms and conditions of
the solicitation may result in the offeror being ineligible for award.
